O, my children, now I have completed this book, which is the last of the science of medicine, by fulfilling its purpose in it, and through the explanations and clarifications within it; to me it seems that I have made difficult for you to understand this treatise, which is part of the operation as I know it, that is, surgery.
For the practice as I know it is deprived in our region and in our time of everything, except that the science of it has become rare, and its practitioners have diminished; and we find only small descriptions of it in the books of the Ancients, which have been altered to such an extent that they contain errors and hesitation, obscuring the intentions of the practice and weakening the power and art.
And it seems to me that I should vivify this treatise according to its order through the way of explanation and clarification and abbreviation; and by presenting the forms of cautery tools and other instruments used in the work as they are with added descriptions and preparation, which is necessary.
But the reason why a good craftsman is not readily found in my time is that the art of medicine is extensive, and it requires the practitioner to be well-versed in anatomy, which includes knowing the functions of the members and their forms, as well as their conjunctions and separations; having knowledge of the bones, nerves, and arteries, including their number and distribution; and understanding the locations of veins and where they pulsate.
And for this reason Hippocrates said that in name there is much, but in deed little, and especially in the art of the hand.
This we have already said at the beginning of this book; for whoever is not versed in what we have said about anatomy will not be free from error by which men may die, as I have seen too many of them, for some are formed in this science and forget what they know and what they have experienced.
For I saw a physician who foolishly cut into an abscess in the neck of a woman, and he cut some arteries in her neck so that much blood flowed out, and the woman died because of it.
And I saw another physician who attempted to remove a stone from a man who was suffering from kidney stones, and the stone was large. He came to him and extracted that stone along with a piece of the bladder, whereupon that man died on the third day.
And I had already called to remove that stone and saw that because of the size of the stone and the condition of the patient, I knew for certain that he would die.
And I saw another physician who received payment from a duke of our land to perform surgery on a black castrated man who had a fracture in his chest. Because of the physician's ignorance, he removed the splint over the wound and applied poultices and bandages with strong pressure, without allowing air circulation to the wound.
And he was loosened according to his desires, and then he was relieved, and after some days, he commanded us to loosen the bandage. And thus it happened that the chest and the arm became abscessed, and he came to ruin.
And I was called to him, and I prepared to remove the bandage, and as a result, he found peace and relief from his pains.
However, if corruption was confirmed in the limb, so that it could not be restrained, and the corruption did not cease to spread throughout the limb until the patient was in danger.
And I saw another surgeon who incised a cancerous abscess, and it ulcerated near the armpit, until the malignancy spread throughout the body of the lord of the manor.
The cause of which is that the malignant cancer is pure of melancholic humor; therefore, it does not need to spread throughout the entire body, but rather remains in the member that can endure such affliction.
And for this reason, children, it is necessary for you that the operation be devised in two aspects: one is an operation associated with health, and the other is a deed in which there is risk even under the best circumstances.
And I have established this in every place in this book where there is an operation involving error and fear; therefore, it is necessary for you to keep this in mind and avoid that, so that the pages do not find a way to speak ill of me and dishonor you.
And so take up your arms with diligence and the protection of God, and treat your patients with skill and firmness.
And use the best path by God's grace to lead to health and praiseworthy success, and leave aside terrible diseases that are difficult to heal, and remain armed against what causes you fear, so that hesitation in your faith and in your name does not betray you: for it is better to remain in your glory, and later in the world and at the end of your sanctity.
Wound treatment in some monastic surgeries: Do not treat illness badly, for thus bad doctors are not named.
And I have devoted this book according to three chapters.
Begin the division of the book, and first of the first part. The first chapter is ordered about the head within, in the forms of the instruments and in the tools of the cauteries, and of what is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, about cutting and piercing, and about suction cups, and plasters, and the extraction of arrows and similar things, all chaptered and ordered by the forms of the instruments.
The third chapter, about restoration and dislocation, and the treatment of twists and similar things; a chapter ordered about the head within, and of the forms of the instruments.
I will speak about the quality of the actions of that cautery and of its ingredients, and in which condition cautery is prohibited.
Therefore, I say that the speech about the quality of the action of cautery and its ingredient is long and tedious, subtle by knowledge, and hidden as a secret; and many wise people have spoken about it, and they are disagreed on this matter, but for me, a little of their speeches is enough to avoid prolonging.
Therefore, I say that cauteries conform to all complete formations universally, whether they have material or not, except for two formations, which are tail formations without material.
In the dry tail formation with material, it dries out; for some say that cautery is helpful in this case, and others say the opposite, that cautery is not appropriate for a disease that is due to quality and dryness, because the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and it is inappropriate to treat a dry tail formation with something as hot and dry.
And those who say the opposite are wrong, that by cautery there is help in all dry and tail diseases that occur in human bodies, for when you compare the human body and its humidity to the nature of fire, you find that the human body is cold.
And I say according to the speech of that person, that experience has already shown this to me on several occasions.
But it does not suit someone who has already been taught and trained in the chapter of cauteries by previous practice, and who has known the diversity of human formations and the disposition of diseases in their seasons, and the causes of those diseases, and their accidents, and the time span of them.
But in the other formations, there is no fear for you, especially in cold and humid diseases, since all doctors are already in agreement about those, and they do not disagree on the use of cautery in such cases.
And you know, children, that the secret of healing by cautery with fire and its goodness is that fire is simple, and its action affects only the member that is cauterized and does not spread to other members unless it is applied to them, causing only minor harm.
Here is the English translation:
Keep the fire, by its high position and the goodness of its substance, does nothing but cause superfluity. And it is known to us through experiment and the length of service in studying the art regarding the truth of causes; and for this I excuse myself from the length of speech. And if not that it would not be read in my book, at this pause I hide from you secrets about fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies and the expulsion process by which you expel diseases, with philosophical demonstrative speech, which would sharpen your thoughts.
And know, children, that they disagree about the time when it is convenient to perform cautery and they pause at the best time of spring.
And I say that cautery is convenient at all times, because the harm caused by accidental circumstances of time is submerged in the benefit brought about by what is drawn from the cautery, and even more so if the cautery is for pains or necessary pain, strength and boils, which cannot tolerate delay due to the fear of malice, which is worse than a small injury entering through the time.
And this does not concern your thoughts, or, children, only the common people and foolish doctors think that for the disease that is cured by cautery, it is not necessary at all times, and they pause at that consequence.
And the reason is not as such that they believe this, because cautery is nothing but a substitute for medicine that alters the complexion and dries up the humidity which is the cause of the pains.
But keep in mind that cautery is excellent above medicine due to the speed of its effectiveness and the virtue of its operation and the greatness of its lord.
It is possible that his illness may return at some time according to the condition of the patient and the location of his illness, and its nature, and what has been prepared in his body by the accumulation of superfluities within him, and what has been acquired in it through food and similar causes; but if the illness in which cauterization is administered is a subtle one in a member with few superfluities and humidities, such as cauterization of a tooth for pain and similar cases, it is possible that the pain will not return to it, but this applies only slightly.
And the common saying is that cauterization is the last remedy of medicine, and it is said by practitioners, not because they understand it, but because they believe there is no cure that benefits from medicine or any other cause before cauterization.
And the cause is contrary to that; and the understanding that cauterization is the last remedy of medicine is only when we administer methods of treatment for certain illnesses, and those medicines are ineffective, and at the end of the cause, cauterization is administered, and it proves beneficial then. And now I say here that cauterization is not the last remedy of medicine, not according to the understanding which I grasp of the common and excessive practices of foolish doctors.
And the ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and its superiority in substance.
And they said that the location for cauterization does not matter, which is absolutely not true, for I have already experienced this and found that it works differently on different bodies; in some cases, using gold for cauterization is good and better than using iron as they say. However, when you use fire to melt gold for this purpose, it is not clear how much to use due to the hardness of the gold, and it requires preparation to receive friction. If you place some thin sheets over the flame, the gold will melt from the heat, and in this way, the craftsman can work with it.
And thus is made the cautery of iron, which should be applied gently and gradually according to the correctness of the procedure.
And I have arranged this chapter on cauteries according to the chapters, and I have placed those of the head among the important ones, so that I alleviate the difficulty for those asking for what they want.
The first chapter.
This cautery is applied to the head for the accidental condition caused by cold and humidity, which are also causes of weakness, rheumatic fluxes called chilblains in the parts of the face and ears that weep, excessive sleepiness, toothache, and throat pain, as well as generally all diseases that come from coldness, such as paralysis, apoplexy, and similar conditions.
The form of this cautery is as follows: First, command the patient to evacuate their bowels with a laxative medicine for three or four nights, according to the strength of the patient and their age and usual habits.
And then command him to shave his head with a razor, and then place him seated on a tilted bench so that he rests his head on his hands.
And then place the palm of your hand near the eyebrows on the shaved part of the nose between the eyes. But when the temperature of the middle part has been felt, mark that place with a probe, and then apply the olive cautery, which is made as follows:
And approach him on the side marked for the incision, in such a way that it descends, with which the skin may be gradually stretched, and you turn him.
And lift your hand gently and look at the place, and if you see any amount of bone already exposed, as much as the quantity of grain in one's palm, then raise your hand, and if not return your hand to that tool, or another like it, if it is cooled, until you can see the bone as I have told you.
And then take a little salt and dissolve it over the place and leave it for three days.
And then place on the wound a pad soaked in broth and leave it there until the burn scar is destroyed. And then treat the place with a quadruplex ointment until it is healed.
And when it is said that if the wound remains open, it heals better and is more beneficial, then let the arm be kept exposed.
And some of them say that the wound should be cauterized down to the bone, and that the cautery should be kept until it adheres to some part of the bone.
And then remove what is adhered to the bone, and then it should be treated.
And others say that with the cautery it should reach to the depth where it presses firmly on the bone until the bone softens, and this is the method of alpeccati (likely a typo for "alveccati" or similar term) in a small manner: And from that place exhale the vapors of the head.
And if the wound has been infected for a long time, it should be treated before it is fully consolidated.
But I have not seen these two species of cautery in all cases, only in some people due to a certain method of fear; and one leaves that, in my opinion, it is better for health when it is so; for the head is easily affected by the disruption of continuity as we have testified with other members, and especially when the patient's constitution is cold.
And the first species of cautery is safer and better in my opinion; and from that one uses it for the benefit of health.
Chapter Second.
Of cauterizing the head.
When chronic and long-lasting pain occurs throughout the head and this is prolonged in the patient, and one uses plasters, poultices, compresses, ointments, baths, and other remedies, especially if it has already been cauterized with a cautery that we have described but to no avail from those causes, then consider whether the constitution of the patient's head is strong by nature; and if it is not cold and there is no great tendency towards inflammation, at that time one should cauterize again with another type of cautery after some interval. And then cauterize that spot on the crown of their head with a cautery before the condition becomes worsened. Incise the affected area and expose the amount of bone that we have described, and cauterize it with a cautery at the back part of the head in the place called "vas," — which is the location where the vein is situated. And approach it in this way, and do not expose the bone, for the patient will thereby come to feel great pain different from the pain of all other cauteries of the head.
And here I shall describe this cautery in its place, for it is necessary that the cautery with which you cauterize the horns of the head and the occiput is a finer cautery than that with which the middle part of the head is cauterized; and this is the form of it.
Chapter Three.
On the Cauterization of Non-Ancient Hemorrhoids.
When there is severe pain in the forehead area, or persistent pain inside the head, the head should be cleansed with medicines, and other treatment should be administered, which I have described in the sections on diseases; and if this does not help, cauterization is then done in two ways: either with a sharp burning medicine, or with iron.
But if you want to use a burning medicine for cauterization, take a piece of amber and scrape it, then hold the ends of it from both sides. And then you should make an incision at the site of the pain on the temple with a scalpel, carefully so that it is done just below the skin, making it hidden.
And then apply pressure to it with a cloth by tightly bandaging it, and leave it like this for three hours; then loosen the bandage and remove the amber, and let the wound be covered for two or three days; afterwards place something cool over the area until the spot becomes warm.
Let the wound be treated with care until it is healed.
And if you wish, use some of the medicines mentioned in the second chapter on burning medicines.
For the cautery, do it according to this method: make fire for cauterization, and this is its form:
and it is called a clamp with nail tips, for its head has the shape of a nail, which has some curvature, and in the middle part there is a small prominence.
And then apply it to the location of the pain, and hold your hand—so that the artery below is not adhered—and rotate the tool gently but quickly.
And if the amount that adheres due to the nature of the tissue is as much as half of it, raise your hand so that the artery below is not adhered, so that there is no flow of blood.
And then soak cotton in salt water and place it on the site, and leave it for three days; and then apply dry cotton around it, and treat it with care until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize at the tip of the radius according to the cautery method, and be careful not to cut the artery in this proper non-traditional procedure.
Chapter four.
On the cauterization of an ancient ulcer.
When you treat an ulcer as we have described in the previous treatment and in the divisions of diseases, and if it does not improve, and sometimes due to the severity of the disease, what has been said about the first cautery with medicine or the cautery with fire is insufficient, then you should ignite the radial cautery until it becomes white. Place it on the site of the pain along a line that is half the length of your finger or slightly more; then raise your hand once and press it firmly so as not to cut the artery but reach the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to guard against the continuation of the jawbone, which is malformed due to chewing, and that the lizard [likely referring to a muscle] does not adhere and the nerves which move it, and that it does not become spasm.
And if it is about the custody and caution of the flow of blood from the artery that is cut, because there is fear in its cutting, especially for one who does not know what they are doing and is not diligent and experienced; and leave the operation to someone else at the beginning.
And here I will come to the recollection of the regimen of blood flow from an artery according to the usual method, in its place in this book.
And if you see this illness does not suffice with these cauterizations and the patient's condition is tolerable, cauterize in the appropriate place of the head as we have recounted, and treat the wound until it is healed.
And if you proceed, administer the cauterizations that we have mentioned in the chapter on the cutting of an artery with a cautery having two edges, and this is a better cauterization and more effective.
Chapter 5.
On the cautery treatment for ear pain.
When pain in the ear occurs due to friction and is treated with laxative causes and with the other treatment that I have mentioned in the division, and if the pain does not improve, now use cauterization. This is the one called puncta, and this is its form:
And approach the puncta to the fire, and move it around the entire ear as a wheel revolves, or in the vicinity of each part if the pain is in that part. Lead the cautery of the hair removal from the ear little by little until you have marked the place with it.
And if the cautery reaches those points throughout the ear, and wherever it does, then take care of the places until they are healed.
Chapter VI.
On the cautery of torticollis.
Torticollis, which is cured by cautery, is nothing but a condition caused by phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases.
Avoid cautery for the type that results from dryness or spasm of the nerve.
When you treat that type of torticollis with herbs and purgatives and other remedies, and your treatment does not relieve the condition, then it is necessary for you to cauterize the disease in three places: the first near the ear, and the second a little further from there at the temple area, and the third should be at the junction of the two lips [likely referring to a specific anatomical point].
And pause your cautery on the opposite side of the affected part, for softening occurs only in the part that appears healthy.
The form of cautery is that you cauterize at the place near the uppermost part of the ear on the right side, a little above the horn of the head, and in the temple area, the length of which should be according to the length of a thumb, and then pause your hand with the cautery until half the quantity of the substance is consumed.
This is the form of cautery, and it is specific to the surgeon, the form of which is set out above. However, what is more subtle is that there is a little bit of what you see; and it is necessary to use the knife instead of excessive coarseness in this little bit.
And then treat the area with water as it was previously processed until it is healed.
Chapter VII.
On the cautery for chronic apoplexy.
When apoplexy is chronic and you treat it with water as we have said and your medication does not cause fever in the patient, then cauterize it with four cauteries: over all the temples of the head; and at one cauterization and the middle part of the head, as we have said; and at one cauterization on the nape of the neck. And the method of the cautery is done as mentioned above.
And it has already been cauterized over the mouth of the stomach; and this is better; and then treat it with water as you have processed.
Chapter VIII.
On the cautery for forgetfulness performed with flame.
It is necessary to give the patient large doses of juniper berries and cleansing pills at the beginning.
And then shave the patient's head completely and place a plaster on the nape of the neck, as described in the chapter on plasters.
And pause at certain points, for that is the method of cauterization. And do this according to the order which I have already mentioned.
And thus if the wound is clean it is well; but otherwise, at that moment apply three cauterizations to the rear part of his head, which descend from the highest part of the head into the part nearest to the neck. And pause between each cauterization for the thickness of a finger, and then proceed with the next cauterization.
But if you prefer and the patient can tolerate it, then apply the cauterization in the middle location; and if you want a stronger effect, then cauterize over both sides.
Then proceed with the healing process; and let the cauterizations be olive-shaped as described previously.
Chapter IX.
On the cauterization of parasites and the softening of the entire body.
Proceed with the cleansing of the head using scissors and as we have discussed; then shave the patient's head, and afterward cauterize in the middle part of the head, on both sides of the head, on the rear part, and with three cauterizations along the spine of the neck.
And if it is necessary in the illness of softening the body to do so excessively and the patient can tolerate it and the illness is severe, then cauterize with four cauterizations along the spine of the back, and finally apply one cauterization inside, just below the shoulder blade, and raise the heat moderately. For one side treat that which is to be healed, and this side let it be olive cautery.
Chapter 10.
On the cautery for epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized unless the epilepsy is due to phlegm.
And therefore, it is necessary to purify the brain of the patient at the beginning of the treatment and to use the other cure that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is severe and tolerates the exception of medicines.
And if it is a child who cannot tolerate medicines, then administer gum ammoniac and masticatory substances that purify the brain, for several days before this, along with the improvement of the diet.
And then shave the patient's head, and subsequently cauterize one area at the middle part of the head according to the previous method, and another cauterization at the occiput of the patient, and on each corner of the head as well. And if the patient is strong and can tolerate it, then cauterize according to the methods I have mentioned, with paralysis and relaxation of the body on the cervical vertebrae and the thoracic vertebrae.
And let it be olive cautery as was previously described.
But if the patient is a child, then use gentle cautery according to this method.
Chapter 11.
On the cautery for melancholia.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted humidity and thick phlegm, then cauterize that area with the cauteries which we have mentioned in the case of paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is excess that inclines towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is humid, then give him to drink something that purifies the brain as mentioned previously in the division.
And then shave the patient's head, and then make an incision properly around the circumference, and then place that [incision] in the middle part of the head.
And let the patient be seated comfortably, and let him be held steady from all sides.
And then apply a liniment; it is more suitable to use an antiseptic ointment made from sheep fat. And warm that [liniment] over the fire with moderate heat as required, which the patient can tolerate when applied. And then apply that [warmed liniment] to the middle part of the head in a circle, and let it be rubbed in.
And do this for the patient once a week according to his regimen until he is healed; or if you prefer, cauterize that area with small points as needed, but ensure your hand is guided by a properly ordered cautery: this is a type of cautery that moistens the brain in equilibrium.
And then place that poultice soaked in ointment or in chicken fat.
Chapter XII.
Of cauterization by water descending upon it.
When it is declared by the signs which I have mentioned in the division that the time has come for water to act upon it, then give the patient water that purifies the head from it, and guard against all humidity.
And let him sweat in baths for several days.
And then command him to shave his head, and cauterize that part where the cauterization should be on the head; and afterwards cauterize that part with two cauteries above two temples if it is the beginning of water descending in two eyes, or from one side if it is the beginning of water descending in one eye.
Inciase the area around the cauterization all the veins and arteries that lead to it; and let the cauteries be at a distance in that part, at the latitude of the temples.
And guard against bleeding when it is cauterized; and if you see blood flowing from him, apply some medicine to that area, as is possible for you.
And I will come to the knowledge that is in the extraction of arteries and the ligation of them and the prevention of bleeding.
And in some cases, it is cauterized on the neck behind two bones with two cauteries deliberately applied.
Chapter XIII.
Of the cauterization of old tears.
When tears from the eyes are old and persistent and travel through veins and arteries that appear in a visible part of the head, and it is verified that this is due to cold phlegmatic excess, then cauterize that area with cauteries as we have recounted in the chapter on the beginning of water descending into the eyes, and one cauterization at the middle location of the head, and two cauteries above two temples, and two cauteries behind two bones in the neck. And if you need an addition, now cauterize that in all the skin of the hand above the extremity of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Chapter xiiii.
On Cauterization of Nasal Discharge.
When you treat him with what we have mentioned in the division and it does not benefit from your treatment, now prepare and give the sick person coriander to drink for three nights; then shave his head, and cauterize him with a moderate olive cautery. And then cauterize him with a moderate clove cautery on both eyebrows above the hair slightly.
And be careful not to burn that area.
And this is the form of the clove cautery.
Chapter .xv.
On Cauterization for Softening the Eyelids.
When the eyelid is softened due to illness or moisture, now cauterize that eyelid with this lunar cautery; and this is the form of it:
And if you do so, cauterize that above both eyebrows slightly with two cauteries in total, and let them extend towards the temples. And let the length of each cautery be according to the quantity of the eyebrow.
And do not press too hard with your hand when using the cautery, but rather so that one-third of the eyelid is adhered.
Chapter XVI.
About cauterizing the eyelid when the hair turns white and spreads to the surrounding area.
When the hair of the eyelid turns white and spreads to the surrounding area, causing pain in the eye, cauterization should be performed in two ways: either by burning or by using a combustible medicine.
If cauterization is done with fire, instruct the patient to shave the hairs as others do, making sure they are long and even; and if pain occurs where the hair grows, then wrap the eyes with a bandage so that nothing interferes until new hair begins to grow.
Once the new hair has grown and is even, then instruct the patient to place their head in a warm position, and gently press on the eyelid where the cauterization was performed, marking it in the shape of a leaf, with the beginning of the mark near the hair.
And then place a small piece of egg white or mucilage of flypaper on the eyelid.
And then perform the cauterization, which has this form.
And then cauterize over the marked figure little by little, in small strokes, until the surface of the area shaped like a myrtle leaf is thoroughly burned.
And the sign of health in this treatment is that you see the eyelid of the eye become contracted and the hair around it raised above the surface of the eyelid.
Then raise your arm and keep it raised for three days, and then pause on the wound edge until the scar is healed. And then take care of it in this way until it is healed.
If the hair returns due to some cause and the eyelid becomes inflamed, then perform cautery on it again just as you did initially.
But if the hair is on the lower eyelid, then cauterize it until it rises to its natural position and heals so that the hair does not touch the eye.
But with cautery and a burning medicine, this is what you should order the patient to do: have the hair extended and healed, and then make from cloth a leaf of myrtle shape.
And then take known soap and one ounce of living oil, or something similar, and mix these oils well, applying it quickly so that it is not rubbed; and spread this over the cloth made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it on both eyes; and cover the eye wound with albumen from eggs, and have the patient's head in your lap.
And place your finger on the medicine and press it gently without moving until the patient feels the stinging of the medicine, as this stinging is like that of fire.
And as long as the burning sensation persists, leave the medicine on your finger and apply it; when the stinging stops, then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water; then check if the eyelid has risen properly after washing, and you should proceed with cautery or incision if necessary; but if not, return to applying the medicine to a place where you have not yet applied it until it heals without discoloration.
Then pause over the cut until the pain of the operation is eradicated, and then treat that which has become inflamed or another condition until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you to guard your operation with diligent vigilance so that no part of the medicine falls into the eye. And if after some days the eyelid becomes inflamed and any cause of hair growth in the eye, then repeat your medication on the place where the eyelid is inflamed, and properly as you did at the beginning, and then around until it is healed.
And this is the form of the mirror leaf.
And know that the eyes of people vary in size and smallness, and therefore according to this you should adjust your treatment.
And the way to treat will not be hidden from one who studies in this art.
Chapter XVII.
On the cautery treatment for a fistula in the lacrimal duct of the eye.
When you treat a fistula with what we have mentioned in the divisions of diseases and do not find success in your treatment, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this method: instruct the patient to place his head in your lap, and hold the head of another person between your knees in such a way that it does not move or shake.
And then place a cut piece of egg white or mucilage of flour on the eye.
Here is the fire for cautery, which has this form:
which should be hollow, like the shape of a reed or the quill of an eagle, at one end of which the cautery is made.
And if you wish, it should penetrate into the other end. And if you want it to be as thin as a thread.
However, the one that is concave is better for this work.
And press the fistula if it is open, and then dry that area. And if it is not open, then open it and extract the putrefaction from it.
And then apply the cautery to it, which should be well heated, and hold it there for a short time but do not bring the cautery near the eye or else you might injure your hand or disturb the malady, and then place the cautery on the gums and burn that area.
And so if at the beginning of your cautery it penetrates to the bone, that is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery once or twice, as necessary; and leave it thus for three days, and then apply a poultice around the area and use an astringent inside until it is healed.
But if after these days it has not healed, then apply a sharp corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed and proceed as appropriate according to its chapter.
And this is another method of cauterizing a fistula, which the ancients first described: Introduce into the place of the fistula and insert there something thin with the form of it. And put in there one ounce of molten lead; and hold your hand well and with good retention, so that not too much of the pus does not pass by such that the molten lead may reach the wall of it; and cover it upon the wall of the fistula cut off in egg white or in water, for lead adheres to the place of the fistula and heals it through wonderful healing.
And if the fistula is healed by what we have said about cauterization and treatment, that is good; but if not, it is now necessary to administer a tragus of the nose and reduce the fistula to the body of the nose according to how it will come to its proper place.

Chapter XXI.
On the cautery for toothache.

Cauterization with a horn is when you take a cow's horn and boil it in iron rust water, then cut cloth and wrap it around the end of the horn. Then immerse the heated horn briefly in cold water, and quickly apply that to the painful tooth before it cools down.
And then repeat that several times until the effect of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, submerge wool or cloth in the aforementioned horn water, and place that on the painful tooth, then place heated iron on it until the iron reaches the depth of the tooth's pain.
However, cautery with fire is such that you should attend to the thickness of the tube or iron so that its inner width is sufficient and the intensity of the heat does not reach the mouth of the patient.
And then heat the cautery to the form it will take, and place that on the tooth with your hand until the cautery cools down; do this several times as the pain subsides either on that day or the next day.

After the pause of the cautery on that mark, hold the cautery straight and enter with it where you can reach the bone of the fingertip within the joint; and repeat on that other side if you did not succeed in the first attempt to reach the bone.
Observe carefully the condition of the bowel during your cautery, so that you do not burn it, lest death or another great harm come to the patient.
And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, do not proceed with your operation.
And it should be that the cautery for children is delicate according to their age and size.
And afterward, treat the site of the cautery for three days with a dressing until the burn scar has healed.
And afterward, treat that with other ointments until it is healed.
And let the patient lie on their back for forty days until the site is sealed and the wound healed.
And it is necessary to restrict the patient's diet according to the duration of the healing period during which the intestines are weak, so that the bowel does not protrude due to excessive strain.
And afterward, when it is time to remove [the dressing or restraint] after forty days, administer it carefully and properly, and keep that in place for another forty days.
And let the patient avoid work and overeating of food and drink, and loud speaking, for when using this complete regimen of healing, they will be healed.
This is about the treatment of ruptures in other parts of the abdomen, and at the beginning, when you do not want to delay, cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size, and it should be as wide as one-third of it; then treat that area as we have said, and no adjustment is necessary.
And some earlier practitioners said that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery in this form, as it is marked with a template:
and draw a line horizontally across the navel above the rupture, and another line above it; then place your hand with a nail-shaped cautery, but the first mentioned cautery is faster and better.
Chapter XLVI.
On the Cauterization of Twists.
When pain occurs in some members due to falling or impact and persists for a long time without being relieved by medicine, then it is necessary to cauterize with a pointed cautery.
And the size of the cautery for each member should be according to its size and smallness, its nature and condition, and the location of the twist and pain.
If it heals with the first cautery, that is good; but if not, then repeat the procedure with the cautery. For it is customary for such pains to be punctured from one member to another nearby one, so you must achieve this with the cautery until the patient is healed.
Chapter XLVII.
On cauterization for leprosy.
Some cases of leprosy are greatly helped by cauterization, but it is not effective for the type of leprosy that arises from the putrefaction of flesh and melancholy.
And therefore, when you want to cauterize that person, consider whether the leprosy is contagious and if it can be cured by what we have mentioned in the division [of cases], and do not proceed unless this is confirmed. You must also be cautious about the possibility of corruption spreading throughout their body and entire complexion. Then cauterize them on the head with a hot cautery: one at the middle part of the head, and another below it near the forehead; place two on each side of the temples; and one at the back, either on the nape or in the hairline.
Finally, press the cautery a little into the skin so that it leaves a small indentation and displaces the scaly layers, thus allowing the expulsion of thick vapors to be eased. Cauterize over the affected areas as required.
And if the leprosy has already spread over the body and is clearly manifested, then you should cauterize those areas with the cauteries mentioned for the head; one on the tip of the nose, two on each cheek, two on each side of the neck vertebrae, six along the spine, one large one near the waist, one on the waist itself, two on each thigh, one on each ankle, two on each wrist, and two on each muscle and tendon of the feet; also cauterize all the joints of the fingers and toes, as well as each heel and the elbows.
And guard against the nerves, especially those on the heel, so as not to burn them.
And sometimes it is cauterized with one cautery on the bone of the pubis and another on the mouth of the stomach, and another on the spleen.
And know that the more you adjust the cauteries, the more beneficial and appropriate they are; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as others do, because the body of the patient is already numbed.
And it is appropriate that the cauteries be large or few according to the limbs and joints, depending on the nature of the tools used.
And properly apply the cautery with flour of oats mixed with honey, and continue the other treatment until he is healed.
Chapter XLVIII.
On Cauterization for Inducing Stupor.
When a limb is numb or asleep and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and does not heal, then you should cauterize that numb limb with cauteries according to the size of the limb.
And let the heat of the cautery enter deeply into the skin a little. And properly treat that area with an ointment until it is healed.
And sometimes numbness in certain areas is cauterized, such as those affecting the thighs and hips, and along the vertebrae of the back, and also the points where the nerves that govern that limb are located, to relieve the numbness.
One should not attempt this except one who is skilled in the anatomy of the members and the emergence of the nerves throughout the moving body.
Chapter XLIX.
On cauterization of ulcers that become indurated.
When ulcers are old and do not respond to any of the ointments of medicine, then you should cauterize over them, and precede this with a little according to the quantity of the substance inside until the whiteness and color change.
And then apply that which is made of flour of oats and lentils with rose oil and leaves of arnica, and the blood of dove or the blood of roe deer, a part of each, and all are mixed together, and then place a cloth on it until it heals.
Chapter L.
On cauterization of cancer.
When cancer begins and you wish to remove it, then cauterize around it in a circular manner as it appears.
And the wise say that it should be cauterized with a hot iron in the middle; but I have not seen this done, for I fear that it will become ulcerated, and I have seen this happen several times.
And it is more appropriate to cauterize around it in a circular manner as we have said, or with moving cauteries.
Chapter LI.
Of cauterization for abscesses.
When an abscess is delayed in maturing, and this is due to the excess of phlegm present there, or because of the patient's condition, being old and debilitated with little blood, or because of the time; then if you wish to hasten its maturation, cauterize around it slightly with a small pointy cautery; and immediately let that which will hasten its maturation be applied.
But if you wish to perforate it with the cautery, then you take the cautery which has this shape; and place it in the middle of the abscess until it penetrates the core.
And if the cautery is applied to a place that is farther away, so that the arm may be spared; and then treat it until it is healed.
Chapter LII.
Of cauterization for corrosives.
A corrosive is a wandering corruption in the limb, which corrodes as fire consumes dry wood.
Therefore, if you see the corrosive in a place where it can tolerate heat from fire, then use cautery with small pointed instruments and larger ones as is appropriate for the location of the corrosive.
And then cauterize it thoroughly from all sides until you eradicate all the corrosion and leave no cause for recurrence.
And then apply treatment for three days, and pause over the cauterized areas thrice daily with oil mixed until all the scars are eradicated and all the corruption is gone.
Regarding the treatment, apply a dressing that generates flesh.
If after three days the flesh is born healthy and there is no corruption, it is good; but if not, then cauterize again over that which is rotten in the corrupted places.
And corrosive is the treatment with certain sharp medicines, for that one serves as an alternative to cauterization. However, cauterization with fire is quicker in producing relief.
And now I have described the treatment with sharp medicine in the division, and so take that when you see an indication for it.
Chapter 53.
On Cauterization of Nails and Other Similar Areas.
Often in the lower parts of the foot there is a malady called a nail, which is hard and protruding, causing pain; and cauterization in these cases can be done in two ways, one with fire and one with hot water.
However, cauterization with fire is done by heating the cautery, which should be concave like a ring, made of iron according to the size that contains the nail on all sides, and it should be smooth.
And then place the heated cautery on the nail, and then rotate your hand with the cautery around the nail until the cautery reaches the depth of the nail. And leave it for three days until pus begins to discharge. Make a plaster with wild mallows torn apart with salt, and leave the plaster on it for one night, for that will eradicate its roots.
And then treat the area with a flesh-generating ointment until it is healed.
And if you do not convert it, and spots appear on the surface of the body, mostly on the hands and feet, then you should administer cautery with water. Take a small tube made of earth or iron or copper, and place it over the wound; then pour some hot water into the tube, and hold it tightly so that you compress it with your hand all around, and let the edge of the tube touch the root of the wound. The hot water will flow towards the point of the root; wait a little for the scalding effect of the hot water for about an hour, then remove it, for the wound with its roots will be eradicated.
And do this with each of them in turn until you cover all the places where they appear on the body.
And then treat the pus where the roots of the wounds have been eradicated with the water from the ointments that generate flesh.
Chapter LIII.
On the cautery of trembling.
When you find that someone trembles due to friction in the nerves or from a fever caused by friction, or from some similar cause, then it is necessary for you to cauterize it with four cauteries or five on the vertebrae of the back, between each vertebra with one caustic; and at the joints of their feet, and above their stomach, use an olive-shaped cautery.
And when the shaking subsides, hasten the health of the patient by friction.
Chapter 14.
On the cautery for various accidents to the body.
When on the body there appear various eruptions, and so pustules and fissures which are formed from gross, corrupted matter; then it is necessary at the beginning as appears to me, that it be cauterized over all the head of the fistula with a fine cautery made of myrtle wood, the end of which is extended towards the fire; or with razor blades of erestologia (a type of reed); or with a lens-shaped cautery.
And sometimes the cautery is applied immediately at the beginning of its expulsion according to this method; and it is not considered excessive, and the superfluity causing those conditions is dispersed, thus healing them.
But it is necessary that this be done near evacuation or phlebotomy.
Chapter 56.
On the cautery for bleeding accidents due to cutting of an artery.
Often when an arterial bleed occurs due to the cutting of an artery because of the plague that is within, or near the beginning of abscesses or cautery of the limb, and in similar cases, it is difficult to remedy that.
Then when such a situation occurs, immediately place your finger at the orifice of the artery, and pause over it with your warm hand until the bleeding of the blood stops, and ensure it does not continue.
Take out of the fire some olive cauteries, both small and large, in number, and blow upon them until they are lit.
Take from them one small or large depending on the location and the condition in which the artery is ruptured, upon that vein quickly before you have bent your finger, and hold the cautery until it is heated and constricted that blood.
And if the blood is expelled from the orifice of the artery when you move your finger and withdraw the cautery, then take another cautery quickly from those which are in the fire and prepared, and thus do not cease to do this one after another until the blood is constricted.
And be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is here, and that it does not cause other harm.
And know that when blood flows from the artery, it is then impossible to constrict the blood in those cases, especially when the artery is large, unless you use one of four methods: either use cauterization as mentioned before, or apply traction when it has not been done, for when it is done, the extremities are burned and the blood is constricted, or bind it with honey or a binding agent due to its strong structure, or place it on medicines whose effect is to restrict the blood; and tighten it with padding and appropriate constriction.
But he who administers appropriate constriction with binding and tightening with cloths or by placing it near burning objects and similar methods should do so cautiously.
But if this happens to someone and there is no doctor present or medicine available, then carefully place your index finger on the opening of that vein as we have said, and understand that with great pressure within, the blood should be stopped from flowing out of the main part of the wound, and do not move your finger over the artery; and sprinkle cold water over it until the blood is congealed and thickened; and then decide whether cauterization or medicine is necessary.
On cutting and piercing and about phlebotomy and plasters and their similarities.
In the first chapter, we have already discussed all diseases in which cautery with fire is appropriate and medicines that promote combustion, as well as the occasions and causes of them, and the instruments necessary for the forms of cauterization; and I have arranged the chapters on the subordination of the head among the parts.
And I will proceed in this chapter in that manner, so that the reader may be praised for understanding what has been asked about.
And before I begin this, listen, son, and learn that in this chapter what is discussed is similar to what was covered in the first chapter on cautery.
And for this reason, great caution is required, because in the operation discussed in this chapter many precautions must be taken regarding bloodletting from veins that sustain life, whether by applying pressure to stop bleeding after an incision on an abscess or opening an exit for pus or cleaning a wound or extracting gravel or starting a stone and similar procedures. And with all of these there accompanies fear and trembling, and in most cases their mistakes lead to death.
And I warn you that this does not fall upon you in which there is hesitation, because some cases depend on your methods of dealing with people and many types of diseases. And among them are those who become enraged by their illness and are close to death because of the vehemence of what they experience from their illness, and due to the length of their illness, and the illness itself brings about fear which signifies death.
And among them is he who gives you his property and says, hoping for that from you health, and the woman's illness is fatal.
And therefore it is not fitting that you consent to him who comes to you in this manner; and your caution should be greater than your greed and your rapacity; and do not presume any cause about this without certain knowledge which verifies what belongs to you, and to whom by succession the commendable praise.
And use in the treatment of all your patients prognosis and indication of him to whom health is converted, for in that is your helper concerning acquisition of fame and memory, of praise and glory.
O, children, may God inspire your mind and not deprive you of direction and protection, for this is in His hands.
And I have arranged this chapter distinctly by chapters as it preceded in the chapter of cauterizations, of the cure of the head among the chest issues, so that you may be pleased with what you seek regarding this and what you need.
First Chapter.
On the treatment of water that is contained in the head of children.
Know that this illness often afflicts children after birth when the nurse presses the child’s head too hard.
And sometimes it afflicts for hidden causes that are not known.
But I have seen this illness only in children; and in all those whom I saw it led to death, and thus it appeared to me as a deadly work in them.
I saw that a child had their head filled with water, and the swelling of their head was so great that a king could not place a crown on it because of the size of their head, and more than that, the moisture caused further enlargement until it became fatal.
And this moisture either accumulates between the skin and the bone, or it accumulates below the bone on the skull.
For if the moisture is between the skin and the bone and the abscess is small, then you should make an incision in the middle of the head with a split in its length, and let the length of the split be about two fingers wide so that the moisture can flow out, and this is the form of the cut:
And if the moisture is greatly increased and the abscess is larger, then at this point there are two incisions made in this manner:
And if the moisture is below the bone, the sign of this is that you see the seams of the head covered all around and the water is squeezed out when you press it with your hand from the outside to the inside, and it does not return immediately. You should make three incisions in the middle of the head in this manner:
and immediately extract all the moisture; then close the incisions with strips and bandages; then apply ointment made of wine and oil starting from the fifth day, and then loosen the bindings and treat the wound with soft cloths and herbs; then cover the head evenly; and manage the illness with dry food having little moisture until the member is strengthened and healed.
And there is another method of incision, which considers the location and collection of water in the abscess, for sometimes it is better at the occiput or in front, or on the right, or on the left; therefore, pay attention to where the abscess appears and the accumulation of fluid, and proceed accordingly as best suits you.
And observe that you do not cut the artery and let blood flow, for the illness may be cured by that outflow of blood along with the evacuation of humidity.
Chapter Second.
When dealing with catarrhs or rheums in the legs or feet, and if this is an old condition, and if the cure cannot be achieved by medicine alone, then the last resort in such cases is to incise those two arteries.
And therefore, when you wish to incise those arteries that the patient uses to touch their head, first rub the area with a rough cloth so that the arteries become visible; then secure the patient's neck with a cloth. Next, feel for the pulse of the vein; these locations are near where the ears would be if they were lower down, and in some people they may be hidden.
And then press on the artery with your thumb, and then incise each one with a sharp knife, making an incision that penetrates slightly into the bone, and this should be done according to the width of the head.
And if you wish, insert the spatum before the artery and cut it where it branches above.
And let the length of the incision be about two fingers wide, for when any vein is cut, the blood spurts out in a pulsating manner, which comes forth frequently.
But if the artery does not appear in the incision, now you should measure from the ear the quantity of space of three fingers, and then sign it with your finger, and make an entry into the bone.
And the amount of blood to be let is a quantity of one vi uncie, and it should be more or less depending on what appears regarding the strength of the patient and the fullness of the artery.
And then consider the condition, and if there remains on the bone any cause of swelling, now cut that so it does not become an abscess from cauterization.
And then strengthen the condition with poultices and bandages of cloth, and afterwards treat it with medicines until it is healed.
Chapter III.
On the extraction of arteries that are in the temples.
When someone suffers from severe headaches or sharp pains due to excessive moisture in the membranes of the temples or hardening similar to that, and is not helped by medicinal treatments, then we resort to the extraction of arteries in the temples or cauterization of those areas as we have shown.
Of the method of the operation and extraction of these is that the patient shave the hairs which are in the temples; and understand to the artery apparent in the temple where it is shown to you by its hair, and is hidden only in few men by vehemence of rubbing.
And if it is hidden from you, then tie the head of the patient with some cloth; and afterwards rub the place with a rough cloth or evaporate the place with hot water until the artery appears clearly. And now you take the spatum which has this form: And then you cut the skin with that which is easy until you reach the artery; and then place it where you intend and extract it to the parts above until you extract it from the skin and reveal those of the tunics which are beneath it, from every part.
But if the artery is fine, then wrap it at the point where it needs to be joined, and then cut a part of it according to the quantity by which the ends need to be lengthened or contracted, and there will not be any bleeding, for if they are not cut as such, the blood will not rise properly.
And then remove about one ounce of blood up to three ounces.
And if the artery is large, then make sure you tie it in two places with strong silk thread doubled or with long cords, and do not allow it to rot before the consolidation of the wound and prevent any bleeding.
And then cut the excess that is between the two ties; do this at that hour or shortly after.
And if you wish, cauterize that which must be cauterized inside the bone which must be cauterized with a knife entering where the extremities of it are incised, and let it remain in place of that part which is to be worked on.
And it is better to perform the procedure if the patient has a fever or is of overheated complexion; for cautery helps to eliminate excessive moisture, and thus is more beneficial in such conditions.
And it is appropriate for the removal of arteries to fill the empty space with pieces of cloth, and place them on powder that has been properly prepared, and nearby apply dry medicines that help flesh grow and use poultices until it is healed.
And if during the procedure there is a sudden flow of blood from the artery, then you should act to stop the bleeding, either by cauterization, or by filling the space with cloth, and press firmly until the blood is stopped. And if none of those causes are present to you, then place your finger on the spot until the blood is constricted, and apply the area with water of extreme coldness until the pain subsides, and press as necessary.
And what is quicker in the removal of an artery is that you cauterize the vein with this cautery having two probes, after you have marked the two spots with thread, and then place some material that ignites within until it reaches the bone and cuts the vein at two points, so that it stretches what is between the extremities, as they are not fully consolidated by this cautery.
And this is the form of the cautery:
And so let the sharpness of both blades be tested. However, if the sharpness of one instrument is better than that of two blades, because even though they are very sharp like two blades, it approaches each incision without cutting the flesh too quickly.
Therefore, when there is any swelling, the heat of the fire should be applied to it, and the flesh should be excised quickly.
And this method is better than all other methods and faster.
And let the space between two blades be the width of a finger.
Chapter Four.
On the treatment of sharp and acidic tears from the eyes.
When there are acidic tears, it is due to the condition of those veins which are above the head, and if no cause for treatment with medicine is found in this, the face of the sick person may become red, and a feeling like ants crawling can be felt on their forehead. The eyes from that point become very tired, and the moisture in them becomes so noticeable that even the hair around the eyelashes can be seen clearly. The eyelids are burned by the sharpness of the tears, and in treating this condition, ancient practitioners often used a specific method which was quick to effect.
And what you command is for the sick person to shave the hair on their forehead, and then make three incisions evenly spaced according to the length of the forehead. And if the length of each incision is about two fingers: one incision should be made evenly in the middle of the forehead at a distance equal to the length of the nose, and the second according to the length slightly toward the direction where the tears flow from the lacrimal area, and the third on the opposite side.
And guard against the beginning of the arteries, which are in two parts, and extend your hand along the continuation of both jaws. And if the space between each incision is the quantity of three fingers adjusted.
And if you have a piece of prepared sponge or dried cloth with which you can dry the blood.
And then insert the spatula between two sharp points, which is the form of the incision as follows: which is from the edge of the plate to the second incision. Excise from there all the tissue that is between two incisions at the cifrad (a term likely referring to a specific anatomical location), and then make this median incision to the second incision. And then stretch with this spatula and insert into the first incision another tool called a cutter, sharp on one side and not sharp on the other.
And hold the sharp side against the adjacent flesh and the curved side within the bone, and insert it until you reach the median fissure, and dissect all the vessels that descend from the head to the thighs.
But ensure that the incision continues along the appearance of the tissue, and then make this in the median fissure to the other fissure.
And when the flow of blood is moderate, press the areas where the clotted blood has collected.

Chapter 5.
On the treatment of headaches through catharsis and the expulsion of humors from the inner parts of the head.
When you encounter acute and continuous bloodletting, and sometimes the patient's humors are weakened and small, and if their condition shows debilitation, and the eyelids are ulcerated with hair loss, and there is severe pain in the temples of the head along with extreme dryness, then from these signs you should understand that the matter and catharsis do not come but from veins located in the inner parts.
And the best treatment for these conditions is as follows: command the patient to shave their forehead, and then make a small incision in the middle of the forehead (beginning from the left temple towards the right temple; this incision should go through the bone; extend your hand between the temples where chewing muscles are located), until the bone is exposed.
Dry all the blood with a sponge or dry cloth and then fill between the two lips of the incision with hot oil or lint. And then apply powder mixed with oil and vinegar on top to prevent the formation of an abscess or sore.
And when you remove this and see that the abscess has already diminished, then cover it by rubbing the bone where new flesh begins to grow, and thereafter treat it with a drying regimen that promotes new flesh growth. For example, take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of aloes wood powder, mix them together, and make a plaster from this mixture to be applied to these wounds until new flesh forms.
Chapter VI.
On the treatment of what affects the ears.
Any cause that affects the ears is one of four types: either it is a mineral stone or a cause similar to a stone, such as iron or wood, or it is from a plant, such as thorns or beans, or it is a fluid cause such as water and sour wine or their like, or some animal.
And when a stone or any other cause similar to those mentioned affects the ear and causes pain, expose the ear to the sun, and if you see the stone, then drip into it some substance like violet oil or cumin oil, and shortly afterward administer its extraction under certain conditions, and make them sneeze by inducing a condition, and plug the nose upon the occurrence of sneezing. And then place around the ear some pieces of cloth or wool, and stretch the ear upward to the sides, as movement over several days is helpful in dealing with these causes.
And if it is not expelled, then administer its extraction with an instrument called a gentle epistome, which has the following form:
And if it is expelled with the instrument, that is good; and if not, then administer its extraction with a fine piece of linen through gentle pressure.
And if it is not expelled by any of the above methods, then make a tube of reed and insert one end of the tube into the ear canal, and seal around the tube with wax and softened oil so that nothing enters except through the tube. From there extract the vein with strong traction, for troops watched as we have recounted.
If it is not forced in this manner, now take a thin thread or a piece of equipment with which birds are caught, a small amount, and place that at the end of the vein, and then wrap around that part properly placed. And then insert it into the passage of the ear with ease, and then dry the ear of its humidity.
And if it is not forced by all the causes that we have recounted, now you should proceed to cut that part before it becomes an abscess or spasm.
And the method of cutting that part is that you first puncture the malady of the vena sephasica and extract the blood according to the manner of its nature, and then make it cut between your fingers and turn the ear toward the upper parts, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where it is most pressed. And let the incision be of a lunar shape until it reaches the stone, and when the stone is found, remove it if you can with appropriate instruments; then close the incision at that moment quickly, and care for it until it heals.
And if the cause lying in the ear is one of the grist that grows and becomes inflamed, now administer the treatment and the extraction of it; but if you do not proceed accordingly, then take some fine cotton according to this form: and administer the removal of that grain which is lodged in the ear.
If you do not want to use water when you think that it has already been moistened by the vapor of the atmosphere, place it in several places, and press out from those at the joints or with fine strokes, or as we have said about incision, for pressing out is gentle.
In the water that has entered into the ear, it is useful for the patient to use sneezing at the beginning with certain conditions, and fill his own ear with some old cloth, and place over that ear in which there is the water. If this causes it to be expelled by force, it is good; if not, then take small pebbles or stones according to the length of a finger, and heat those in the fire for a little while, and let the patient insert one of them into the tragus of his ear and jump on that side, and strike with another stone upon the stone which is inside the ear. Do not remove the stone inside until all the water has been expelled.
Do not remove the stone inside until all the water has been expelled. And the water will be expelled in this way that you take paper or tow, and put one end of it into the ear and extend the other end towards the fire until most of it is burned.
And place another piece of tow and do this as many times as necessary until all the water is expelled, and press it with a cannula as was said above about removing the stone.
In the extraction of an animal entering into that ear, if it is a small object, treat it similarly as we have said in the division; but if it is a large object causing pain to the patient, then administer the extraction with strokes and by pressing at the joints, and the cause of this is more serious than all other causes that occur in the ear.
In the extraction of worms generated in the ear, when you treat it with that which we have said in the division and in the chapter on distillations and do not confer your treatment, now you must guard the ear from the sun.
And therefore if any cause of the worms appears, now extract them with gentle movements or subtle instruments; but if no cause appears, now take a cannula below narrow and above wide, which has this shape: And insert the slender end into the ear according to the quantity that suffices for the patient; and then suck it out with strong suction, and do this several times until all the worms are removed.
But if you do not follow the instruction, now plug and seal around the cannula with wax as we have said; then administer distillations that have already been proven effective in treating worms, and you will find this in the chapter on distillations.
And make your application with the instrument with which you pour medicinal oils into the ear, and this is the shape of it: And make it of silver or ivory, narrow at the bottom, in which there is a small hole, and flat on top.
And therefore it should be like pressing against the curvature of the cannula where it will be necessary. And if you wish, take a reed and wrap the end of it decently with cloth, and then pour oil into the cavity of hearing, or juice of some herb, or any of these medicines into the cannula — and that is in the ear —, and then insert the reed with the cloth on top and press it with your hand moderately so that the oil is expelled into the cavity of hearing and the patient feels the oil inside.
And let that which is to be inserted into the ear be already heated over the fire a little. And be careful that the cause for which you will distill into the ear is not too harsh, for medicines for the ear do not tolerate that.
Chapter VII.
On the treatment of blocked ears.
Sometimes some children are born from their mothers' wombs with unopened ears, and this also happens in some adults, where the ear canal is blocked by infection or flesh growing there; and this blockage sometimes occurs at the entrance of the ear canal which cannot be seen, and sometimes it is in the outer parts.
And that which occurs at the entrance of the ear, which cannot be seen, is in the most difficult conditions to heal.
And in that case where you can see it, make sure to expose the ear of the patient to the sun and observe it. And if you see an obstruction that is visible, open it with a fine spatula of this form:
If the end of it where it is narrow, one part being sharp and the other not; and the spatula should have two blunt edges so that it does not hurt the ear.
And if the blockage is due to flesh growing in the ear or in the ear canal, then use fine scissors and cut it firmly but gently until all the flesh is removed.
And if there is an obstruction in the ear canal, now take a thin reed and heat that in fire for a little while, and then put that into the ear canal.
And if you find an obstruction with what the patient finds difficult to hear due to hearing difficulty, exert pressure on it gently; and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear.
And then place in the ear a piece of cloth according to the quantity of the wax that you have wrapped in Egyptian cotton; and do this for several days until you are sure of the consolidation of the obstruction; or take something and soak it in vinegar and sprinkle finely powdered substances over it and use it; and if you see the ear already inflamed, now you should extract what you used and replace it with another thing that you wrap in cerotic wax mixed with rose oil until the inflammation subsides; and then care for it until it is healed.
But if there is a bleeding, now soak a sponge or cloth in cold water and place it on the ear, and use another treatment that stops the blood flow, which is described in the chapter on distillation.
Chapter VIII.
On the treatment of stitches that occur on the eyelids.
Stitches that occur on the eyelids sometimes appear moist, and at other times they are dry.
Therefore, you should have those available in small containers or jars, and then scrape off the scabs with a spatula, and then sprinkle finely powdered substances over the affected areas.
If pain and bleeding come from a vein, then at that moment you should cauterize those that can be cauterized with a fine cautery.
And the best cauterization is near the incisions and troops that return when there remains any cause for them; and when they are cauterized with fire, those causes are consumed and do not return.
Chapter IX.
Treatment for an ailment that affects the eyelids.
Recurrent conditions that occur in the eyelids due to some cause that is similar to a severe ailment in its strength and hardness, and therefore it is called severe.
And it is an aggregation of thick humidity in the eyelid, both above and below.
Therefore, the procedure in such cases is to consider at that moment whether the ailment has appeared on the surface of the eyelid and affects it entirely; and the cause of this is light.
Therefore, place something over that area along the length of the fissure, and then carefully remove it entirely with ease until you can see clearly, and then suspend it with an ointment and cover it.
And if the condition is severe, then you adjust it with stitches; and take care of it until it is healed.
And if it is mild, you will not suffer harm from it because the warmth of the treatment restores and heals it.
And if the swelling is declining towards the inner parts of the eyelid, you should apply a compress to the inside, thereby suspending the swelling until it subsides, and press it from all sides; and if the eyelid due to incision is elongated, this is not noted as a cause for concern.
And after the incision, wash the wound with salt water; and treat the area with something that will heal it until it is healed.
Chapter 10.
On the treatment of abscesses above the eye on the eyelid.
Abscesses are more common in the tissues above the eyelid, and particularly among children, they worsen the eyes of those affected and lead to their weakening; and they cannot bear the brightness of the sun because tears accumulate for them.
And for this reason you see them holding their hands over their faces all the time, and they sleep with their hands over their faces; and thus their eyelids are covered by moist eyebrows, which have been overshadowed by inflammation, and the likelihood of an abscess is apparent in the eye; and when you press the area with your fingers, you can feel tenderness there.
And one method of treatment is for the patient to rest their head in your lap, then place a cloth over it and apply cold to it; make a circle according to the size that contains arternach from all sides, and then place this on top and press with your fingers from all around so that an abscess forms in the middle of the circle; and afterwards drain the moisture within using a spatula inserted along the length of the incision, ensuring that the incision is not larger than what would be made in phlebotomy.
In the main incision cut through the skin completely until you reach the gristle, for in major dislocations you will expose the gristle by a cleft according to the form of white parchment.
Then extract that which you wrapped in the cloths between your fingers from the sides and roll it between your right and left hands until it is spread out.
And be careful not to insert anything into the cleft so that you do not reach the bone with it and damage it.
But if the tendon does not appear at the beginning of the cleft, then insert into the cleft a small probe until you find the tendon; and then extract it as we have said; and then immerse cloths in warm water and vinegar and place them over the area and sprinkle with powder.
And some people sprinkle salt and apply it to the bottom of the cleft so that what remains is dry.
And then care for it until it is healed.
But if an abscess occurs in the area, then care for it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
