And then mark the two prominent points at the end of the probe in the cavity, and join one to the other with a suture.
And then remove the end of the probe, and do not cut through the cavity entirely, nor extend the wound, nor any other cause as I will explain to you in the treatment of an intestinal hernia.
And then treat that as you would treat wounds, and when you incise the abscesses, clean that area and restore the wound until it is healed; for the cavity is contracted and the prominence of rupture is not adjusted.
And cautery is better in this case, for it is closer to healing.
Chapter lxviii.
On the softening of the cord of the testicles.
In many men, the cord of the testicles is softened because the flesh within it is softened, and this requires careful attention.
Then it is necessary for the one who treats this condition to position the patient according to his needs, and to insert the entire cord that is softened over the natural cord; then adjust two edges with suturing.
And if you wish, cut the excess of the softened cord at the beginning with three or four stitches and secure it with a firm suture.
Then incise between the sutures; and afterward, treat for other injuries until he is healed and the wounds have closed.
Chapter lxix.
On Castration.
Know that castration in our law is excommunicated, yet for certain reasons it has been read to me and I remember it in this book; and the remembrance of it is not necessary except in two ways: one is so that when a doctor is asked about it, he knows how to treat someone who undergoes it; the other way is that we have sometimes had need of castration for other animals for our benefit from them, such as horses, oxen, pigs, and similar beasts.
And therefore I say that castration is performed in two ways: either by crushing or by cutting.
In the case of what is done by incision, the way to proceed is that we should cut into the animal in warm water until its genitals are softened and lubricated and hang down. And then take those with your hand inside until they are relaxed and do not appear below the touch.
In the case of castration done by rupture and section, hold the animal and press the root of its testicles with your left hand.
And then lift the suspensory ligaments, and make an incision on each side with two cuts.
And then cut those parts that you will have separated from the rest. And do not leave on those of the penis any excess skin, but rather make the circumcision subtle so that it is above the veins.
And this method of castration is better than the one done by incision, because incision often leaves some part of the testicles which causes the animal to desire copulation.
And then care for the wound until it is healed.
Chapter 70.
On the treatment of hermaphrodism.
Hermaphrodism in men is according to two methods: one is when it appears in the space between the root of the testicles, where there is a figure resembling female genitalia, covered with hair.
And in some cases, that area between the root of the testicles passes urine.
In women there is a special thing: and it is that the knowledge of a woman's part above the pubis is thus like two testicles of a man somewhat round, in the inner part as the scrotum of a man and two testicles.
And the cure is of three kinds: two of them for men and one kind for women. And it is that you should incise those tight muscles within which the infection spreads, and then treat them as you would other illnesses.
And in the second kind of men, where urine is produced in the chain of the testicles, there is no cure or operation for it.
Chapter XXI.
About menstruation and flesh growth due to causes in women.
Menstruation is lightly held due to natural causes, but it is stressed and proper care must be given; sometimes in some women it is magnified to such an extent that it spreads as it does in men and persists during intercourse.
Then it is necessary for you to grasp the excess of menstruation with your hand or with cloth and incise it.
And do not hesitate to incise, especially at the root of the vein, so that it does not cause a flow of blood.
And then treat it as you would other illnesses until it is healed.
Fleshy growth is flesh that appears in the armpit of the woman and slightly extends to the surrounding areas resembling a tail (and thus some call this "tail disease"); therefore, it must be incised as we would do with menstruation, and treated until it is healed.
Chapter LXXII.
On the Treatment of Arthritis.
Arthritis is when the joint of a woman is not perforated or the passage is small. And it is either natural or accidental.
It is accidental due to a previous illness, and that occurs either because the flesh is not properly fitted or due to a thin or thick phlegm.
And it occurs either in the main joint, or in the sides of it, or in the highest part of it, or in the lowest part of it, and it prohibits cooking and intercourse and childbirth, and often prevents menstruation.
And the diagnosis of that condition is made by examination with a speculum, if the obstruction is apparent; but if it is not apparent, then you should search for it with your fingers or with light.
But if the obstruction is due to thin phlegm and it is visible between the two lips, then you should clean and remove that.
And you should place poultices on both lips, and then use your fingers to gently probe from both sides.
And the woman should lie on her back, with her legs spread apart, and then gently stretch both lips to break the thin phlegm and open the obstruction.
And then take wool and soak it in oil and place it on that area, and leave it there for a day to ensure that the incised area heals properly.
If the pus is thick and dense, then at that time you should scrape it out with a reed tube or with a myrtle leaf.
If the obstruction is due to flesh, then suspend that for an hour, and then scrape it out.
And use the medicines that stop blood flow from biting, such as hachetia, dragon's blood, and enses, prepared with egg white.
And then administer a wide lead tube so that the wound does not heal too quickly.
And keep that for several days and administer dry powder.
And then proceed with the other treatment for healing until it is healed.
And in some cases, other tissues become overly large, and then you should incise them according to this method. But if this is due to chronic abscesses, then do not treat the chronic abscess in the flesh in any way that is contrary to the method.
Chapter LXXIII.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids and tumors that occur in the anus of women.
Hemorrhoids are appreciated as the outlets of small veins from which blood flows continuously; and with old hemorrhoids, thrombi are often formed.
And I have already mentioned in the division the types of these and the signs of them, and I will also say which ones receive treatment and which ones do not.
Therefore say that hemorrhoids and piles when they are in the region of the anus and do not appear to the senses, at those times do not be performed treatment with iron.
Those are the ones that are in the opening of the anus, on which one can feel with the sense of touch, those are the ones that can be treated.
And when you place the woman in the position of lying down, clean and approach the pile with scissors, or with a rough cloth, and incise those with a razor.
And then apply a powder to those to stop the flow of blood from one of the incising powders by mastication, such as acacia and similar ones.
And then bind the affected area with a compress for one hour, and then place it in cold water.
And if the flow of blood persists, then apply that area with a decoction of sumac and rind of lemons and gallnuts and similar substances.
And then take flour of barley and compress that area with honey and sour wine and make a plaster on it with the following ingredients.
And if the blood is congealed, that is good; and if not, apply two ventose cups to it, and to the mammary glands with scarification.
And then take wool and soak it in the juice of cilantro or in the juice of linden or in the juice of buckwheat in sour wine and apply it to the location; and then treat the area with ointments until it is healed.
For the treatment of what is inside when it is diseased.
Chapter LXXIV.
On the Incision of the Bladder in Accidental Cases Affecting the Belly.
Various types of abscesses occur in the abdomen, such as inflammatory, stone-related, ulcerative, adherent, gangrenous, carbuncle-like, fistulae, hemorrhoids, and other abscesses. And I have already mentioned these illnesses and the types of them and the signs of them, and their treatments in detail.
And what I say in this treatise about abscesses refers to those that occur in the abdomen when they are of the type that require treatment, and if you want to know how the operation is performed.
Then you must consider whether the pain of the abscess at its beginning is acute with percussion and phlegm and fever, and if there is redness and sensitivity in that area, then do not proceed with incision, but treat it with what helps maturity until the acuteness of the condition subsides.
And now you should have the woman lie on a cushion that has two cushions; let her recline on her back and position her feet below the abdomen, slightly raised, and place her arms with her hands resting by her sides, and secure them with bandages as appropriate.
And then the midwife should stand on the right side and administer the instrument with which the opening of the abdomen will be made, the form of which will be described in the following cases.
And when you want to administer this instrument, place it in the vagina at the entrance of the womb, and let what enters into the womb from the instrument not be more than the length of the vagina itself. If the instrument is longer than the length of the vagina, then you should place pillows against the texture of the vaginal opening so that it is prohibited for any instrument to enter the vagina.
And you should place the spiral that runs along the instrument on its side, so that the practitioner can hold the instrument and rotate the spiral until it is inserted into the opening of the vagina.
And when the area becomes swollen and is touched with the hand and feels hot and moist, then you should dry it using a piece of linen.
And when the discharge is evacuated, then you should place on the wound a piece of cloth submerged in rose oil or green oil, which has some astringent properties; and apply a bandage to the area around the vaginal opening.
And place clean wool over the womb and on the belly, submerged in water in which mallows have been boiled.
And it should be treated properly for about two days using the method that you deem appropriate until it is healed.
And in some cases, the womb and the wound should be washed with this water mixed with honey, and subsequently with water in which lily root or long-leaved arum has been boiled, and then return to the previously used method.
And if the wound is deep inside a damaged womb, then you should be prohibited from treating it with iron, and instead treat it as we have described in the section.
Chapter LXXV.
To teach midwives how to treat malformed fetuses in the manner described according to this non-natural figure.
It is necessary that the midwife knows at the beginning the figure of normal childbirth by signs of light; and it is so when you see the woman strain at her lower parts and desire to smell the air, and she is deceived by what is above her in connection with parturition. When this happens, you will know that this birth follows a natural figure, and the expulsion will be over the head, while the second will either be suspended or hanging from the navel.
Therefore, when you see those signs, then it is necessary to compress the abdomen so that the fetus descends gently, for when it expels the first one with its head, the second will follow, and both should be cleaned of those superfluities by proper cleansing.
However, if it is another type of birth, it is unnatural and not commendable, for when the fetus is expelled on its feet and the body of the fetus is delivered before the head and feet, or one hand or foot first, or the head and a hand or the belly, and frequently turns over its neck, resembling the figures of the unnatural births.
Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in all these matters and to guard against error and deception.
And I show all the figures of those cases, and which kind of birth is in them according to what they signify by that and are placed upon that.
When the fetus is placed upon the woman's head naturally, and it is strongly positioned on the woman and in a difficult place, and sometimes the strength of the woman is weakened, then act so that the woman has it, and evaporate with fenugreek juice and with oily unguents.
And then insert the instrument between those small ribs mentioned, and split it with the second part of the instrument, or dry it with its nail so that you can extract what is inside from moisture. And press the woman's abdomen so that the fetus descends.
But if it does not descend, then have the woman be treated with powder of feathers and powder of fenugreek with syrup.
And then command her, after the treatment, to be made to sneeze with certain conditions; and at her mouth and nose for one hour, because the fetus will be expelled shortly.
And if both parts of the fetus are expelled at the beginning, then you should reduce them to ease little by little. But if it does not obey the instrument, then place the woman on a cushion and lift her feet up, and then strike the cushion on the ground; and have the woman held so that she does not fall due to the impact.
And if the parts are not returned inside and the fetus dies, then incise them and extract the dead fetus or tie the body together with your hand using cloth and extract it gently, as it will be expelled.
When the fetus is cut on its sides, you should then push those parts up, and immediately turn the fetus slightly, and then even it out, and then take a piece of it and stretch those parts little by little.
But when the incision enters into the things, then you command it to be pressed out, and make that person sneeze under certain conditions, for it will come out if God wills.
And if it does not come out with what we have recommended, then you return the fetus little by little until you pause at its second natural position, for it will then come out easily with a slight incision.
And if it is prohibited by all that we have recommended, then take musellage of hartshorn and dissolved gum, and pound it all in the mortar with good pounding, and then apply it to the woman's cervix, at the bottom of her abdomen. And then make the woman sit in warm water, until she reaches the hypochondria.
And when the parts below her are cleansed, then make the woman undergo smoke inhalation of myrtle and pause her for it. And when she has undergone smoke inhalation for an hour, then make her sit on a chair, and then make her sneeze and expel the contents of her mouth, and lift her, and press the part lowest in her abdomen gently, for the fetus will soon come out.
Proceed with the operation longitudinally by lifting one of its parts. Try to reduce the hand, but if you cannot reduce it, then raise the woman and let it go.
And if it cannot be released, then make her lie on the bed, and strike the parts of it vigorously with percussion, and then administer liniments which are soothing and commended for mucilage.
And if labor has begun, then make her sit on the heels, and then study the reduction of the hand, and engage the operation according to its natural figure, and make the woman sneeze and command it to compress itself until it is completed.
Proceed with the operation on the buttocks by spreading its parts and ensure that the bandage is behind its main body. Let the midwife hold the fetus and turn that little one gradually, and let that process be facilitated.
And when it is time and the moment is equal, pause on the part covered with the oil and mucus that we have recommended.
And then command the one who is being treated to turn little by little, and when you have done this, place that thing over a cushion and command them to lean on the right side, and then command them to bend; and make them sneeze under certain conditions. The exit of the prepared fetus on the side.
When you begin the incision of the mother according to this method, consider carefully, and then proceed to make the second cut with your finger so that it is evacuated of moisture.
And if the fetus is suspended over the face and neck of the mother, then you must incise that part of the abdomen so that it is not retained and dies.
And then push the fetus towards the interior parts until you pause at the place that is necessary, and tell the woman to bend several times, and if God wills, it will be quickly expelled.
The delivery of twins or multiple fetuses. Know that twins usually are born in separate births, but sometimes three or four are born at once, though this is rare and difficult to manage; however, these causes are beyond natural occurrence, and not common.
And among these cases, whether they are multiple, make a second incision, and separate them along the ligament at the umbilicus of each one. Sometimes they are born quickly as if it were one fetus naturally and easily, but other times they come out over several births as we have recommended.
And if some are difficult of their births and reach that which we have said about the non-natural figures, then you should care for them as we have recounted.
And if the midwife is subtle and does what she does with both ease and subtlety, and with delay as well, and she acts according to every figure as it is prepared for the birth, aiming at health.
A remembrance of what is formed in the womb from embryos and miscarriages.
Sometimes they are formed in the womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and more than ten, and you should already be convinced that a woman miscarries at six months, and another carries to ten months fully formed, the cause of which is established by measurement according to the glorious wise ones.
And all of this must be known by the midwife because it is very easy to mistake one thing for another, and therefore it is necessary to know what is needed.
Chapter LXXVI.
On the extraction of the fetus when it is dead.
When you care for the dead fetus as we have said in the division of treatment and it is not yet removed, and you are forced to use surgical intervention, then it is necessary to consider whether the woman is of sound constitution and is not affected by any of the accidents that lead to fear of loss.
Now it is necessary for the woman to be placed on her back on the bed with her buttocks raised and her head slightly lowered.
The minister should use a blade with two edges or soak it in oil so that the body does not swell due to the extraction of the stone.
And then moisten the mouth of the wound with olive oil and a paste made of flax, fenugreek, and linseed.
And then the midwife should anoint her hand with those oils and pastes, and then gently insert it into the wound, and then search with her hand for the location of the stones.
And here are the appropriate places for this: then consider whether the stone is prepared to descend over the head of the patient, and if so, place the hooks in the cheeks, or in the neck, or in the mouth, or on the palate, or under the chin, or at the clavicle, or in the regions near the ribs, or under the armpits.
But if the descent is towards the legs, then place them in the groin, or in the middle of the ribs.
And it is necessary to hold the hook with the right hand, and place the curvature of it in the spot between the fingers of the left hand, and gently insert the hand with ease and place the hook in one of those places we have mentioned, until it reaches the hard mass.
And then place and fix in position another hook, or a third if necessary, so that the traction is equal, and not excessive according to its straightness alone.
And be careful at every part, so that the extraction of it is eased as if it were done like pulling a tooth.
So cover with water that which is between them so that the extension may be softened; and if any part of it is held back, then cover so that the midwife anoints some of her said ointment with oil and mixes these thoroughly and rolls in these that which is held back.
Then if the part of the fetus is protruding, now the hooks should be interchanged in the place which is more suitable; and do this until all of the fetus is delivered.
But if the hand is dislocated before the other one, and it is not possible to reduce it by manipulation, then cover with a cloth; and subsequently extract it until all of it is delivered, and cut either that or at the joint of the hand or elbow.
And do the same for the other hand and both feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or there is difficulty in delivery due to stiffness, or it is stuck by the tight fit of the water, then cover and place between the said spined instruments and cut the head and extract the water, or use an instrument called “alundat,” the form of which will be among the forms of other instruments in the chapter that follows this one.
And similarly proceed if the fetus has a large head by nature: then it is necessary to cut that with something sharp, or use an instrument called “alundat” as we have said; and subsequently extract the bones with forceps.
And if the head is stuck and is obstructed by the clavicle, then it should be cut so that the moisture which is in the joints may be effused.
If it is not complicated, nor does it lead to swelling, then cut open the head as soon as it is convenient for you.
And if the parts of the abdomen are pus-filled or are in a state of hydrops, then you should puncture that part through which flows the moisture that is within.
But if the feces are in the upper intestines, then the attraction of it is light and the direction of it towards the mouth of the mother is easy.
But if it is constricted in the abdomen and thighs, then you should remove that cloth with which you have wrapped around your hand, and cut open the abdomen and thighs through which flows what is within them.
But if the other members remain stationary and only the head turns, then insert your left hand; but if the mouth of the mother is open, then insert your hand into the passage, and search for the head, and pull it together with the others into the mouth of the mother, and then insert one or two fingers, and pull them out.
And if the mouth of the mother is constricted by an abscess that has occurred in her, then you should not apply anything heavy to it; instead, you should administer effusions of moist and fatty substances. And apply plasters; and follow with waters that soften and moisten.
And if the fetus is on its side, then if possible, it should be turned; and what we have said about the living fetus should be administered.
And if it cannot be done that way, then it is cut into pieces and extracted.
And do not leave any cause for the second one to occur.
And when you have completed the entire operation, now administer what we have said about the treatment for abscesses similar to those that occurred previously.
And if bleeding occurs, then apply styptic waters and administer the other treatment.
And I have seen a woman in whose womb there was a dead fetus, and above that a second pregnancy, and above the dead fetus another focus of infection. It happened to one who had an abscess in the navel area for a long time; it became internally swollen and filled with pus, and began to discharge pus.
And I was called to treat him, and treated him for a long time, but the wound did not heal.
Then I applied to him some causes of strong attraction and extracted one bone from him, and after passing a few days, I extracted another bone; and I was very surprised, as there were no bones in the abdomen.
And then I thought that they were from the bones of the dead fetus.
Then I examined the wound and extracted several bones from her, the woman being in her confinement period, and thus treated her for a long time, correcting her with a little pus.
And I did not find it strange, since in such cases there is knowledge and assistance for what the skilled physician administers for treatment.
Of the forms of the instruments which are necessary for extracting the fetus.
Form of a spiral used in the major incision:
This is the form of a retractor in which it equalizes the leaves, to this equalization there are two spirals at the ends of two arms. However, this spiral should be finer than the string, and it should be made of copper or the wood of a tree.
And the width of each arm should be two fingers, and the margin of each side should be one finger, and the length of each is half a palm and a little more; and in the middle of the two arms there are two adjustments of the same type of wood that are already fixed, whose length is half a palm plus a bit more, and the width of each is two fingers or a bit more.
And these two attachments should be inserted into the opening of the major incision so that they are opened when you revolve the two prescribed spirals.
Another similar form, finer and lighter:
It should be made of copper or wood, similar to the form of forceps. However, at the end of each of these two attachments, as you see, the length of those attachments is one palm, and the width of each is two fingers.
And when you want to open the major incision with these, then you lay the woman on her back with her legs hanging down, and insert what is between the thighs. Open your mouth and take the tool in such a way as you would with scissors, equally according to the quantity that you want from the width of the larger opening until the measuring instrument does what you want.
The form of dizziness, which the ancients described:
Form of impulse in which the action is pushed forward:
Form of friendship in which the head is contented
And it is similar to forceps, at the end of which there are teeth, as you see. Sometimes it is made long like forceps according to this form, as you can see. At the end, it has teeth like those of a saw, with which incision and holding are performed. Form of friendship for few:
Form of a clamp having a spine:
Form of a clamp having two spines:
Form of a spatula having two ends at which the head is divided:
Form of two broad spatulas:
All those instruments are exercised, and when their various types are multiplied and prepared by the artisans, it is more convenient for their operation and more suitable for people according to their needs.
And do not neglect to prepare any of those instruments, wherever you may be, because the need for them is unavoidable.
Of the extraction of the second [molar]
When the second [molar] is retained after childbirth, you should order the patient to hold their breath, and then cause them to sneeze by tickling their nose, and press your hand over their mouth and nostrils; if it comes out this way, so much the better.
And if not, then take a cloth and make a hole in it, and place it over the mouth of the mother along with herbs such as colchicum, rue, anise, chamomile, Arabian saffron, cinnamon, and sage. All of these herbs or some of them should be submerged in water in the cloth, and place that over the fire.
And then place a reed tube in the mouth of the mother, and keep it there until the vapor reaches the cavity of the mother.
And then cause her to sneeze as we have said, and the second [molar] will be quickly expelled.
But if this cure is delayed and it does not come out, then you should instruct the midwife to immerse her left hand in sesame oil or almond oil, and then insert that into the womb and search for the second [molar] with it. When you have found it, take it out little by little. If it is stuck to the membrane of the mother, then proceed as we have recommended, and when she finds the second [molar], extract it slowly so that the mother does not fall due to strong traction. Take care that it is turned to the right and left with ease.
And if the mouth of the mother is constricted, we have already recommended treatment through sneezing and medication of the wound with herbs.
But if it is not expelled by all the causes that we have recommended, then you should guard against overworking on that which results from placing what has been extracted to the mouth of the mother into the woman's body; and subsequently treat that with cleansing and tetrapharmacum; for this will cause that thing to be reduced in size over a few days and it will dissolve and be expelled.
But when it is reduced, it should be raised from the lower abdomen to the head and to the stomach, which alleviates the illness; and then fumigations and appropriate treatments should be administered for this.
But some of the Ancients already used fumigation with natrtle and dried figs.
Form of an instrument with which the woman is fumigated after the retention of menstruation and during the second half of her menstrual cycle:
It should be made of wood or metal.
And the finer end should be placed in the vagina and the wider end above the fire, and the fumigation should be placed on the coals of the fire.
And keep it inside until the fumigation is consumed and then repeat it with another one.
Of the treatment of the unopened anus of a child.
Some children are born with their anuses not open, which is narrow and closed. Then it is necessary for the midwife to carefully open the mentioned passage with her finger; and if not, she should pierce it with a sharp spatula, being careful not to touch the rectum.
And then apply powder mixed with vinegar and oil; and afterwards, treat the area with an ointment until it is healed.
But if you fear that it is obstructed, then insert a cannula for several days, and remove it when the child needs to defecate.
And if an obstruction of the anus occurs due to the hardening of a sore or abscess; then it is necessary to incise that hardening, and afterwards treat it as we have said regarding treatment and lead.
Of the treatment of fistulas that occur below.
Fistulas that occur in the lower part near the anus are usually hard and thick, which develop close to the anus or in the area between the buttocks.
And it is one fistula or multiple.
And as that hardness becomes old and discharges watery white pus or subtle purulence, sometimes these fistulas penetrate deeply.
And these deep-seated fistulas are known by what is discharged from them through excretion and flatulence; sometimes the bad odor of excretion indicates that they are very severe.
Of those fistulas, some extend into the space penetrating into the bladder, and into the shaft of the penis; and others penetrate into the joint of the thigh and into the root of the penis.
And in the one where a penetrating and non-penetrating fistula is known, you should insert your finger into the anus, and gently introduce a slender probe of wax or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
But if there is tortuosity in that area, now introduce a slender probe of lead or horsehair into it until you feel the probe or the hair with your finger.
And if you do not feel any of this nor proceed with the treatment to find any cause of evacuation such as worms or gas, as we have said, then you know that it is non-penetrating, and now attend to its cure.
And when the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or into the shaft of the penis, then the significance of that is the presence of urine from there and it should be prohibited to do anything that would hinder the healing process.
But if it is penetrating into the joint of the thigh or into the bone and there is pain in the circumference, then the sign of that is that the probe passes here if there is no tortuosity within the bone, and there is pain in the circumference of the affected area; and you will have weakness permanently; and that does not respond to treatment, nor does it heal easily.
And in all those penetrating fistulas, there is not a complete cure, and the treatment of these is laborious and futile for many physicians, which is well established.
In that which is not penetrating and not ancient, healing with iron is hoped for as I shall tell you, and this which I now say.
And it is that the patient should lie between your thighs with his head down and raise his hips up, so that things are inclined towards his belly, and then insert a probe of lead or iron if it is in an ulcerated tortuosity, until you know where the probe passes.
And if that is around the anus, then it is necessary for you to insert your index finger into the anus.
And if you feel with your finger that the probe has already begun to penetrate on its own, or what you feel between your finger and that tissue or flesh, then you know certainly that it is penetrating; and then do not work on it, because there is no healing in that, as we have said.
But some might say that it heals in some men slowly.
And for the treatment by which help is hoped for in him, you should ignite a cautery subtly according to the size of the fistula, as has been described, and insert that heated instrument into the fistula until it goes around the anus; and then repeat this two or three times until you know that all those inflamed tissues are constricted like a feather quill.
And then treat that with bandages wrapped in butter until all those constricted tissues heal, and then treat it with medicines that generate and consolidate the flesh, and if it heals, that is good; and if not, then it will not heal at any time by another treatment.
And if the probe enters and does not penetrate inside; you say which is in the anus, and between that and the probe which is a membrane of flesh or of leather, sometimes the fistula is on that part where the surface of the intestine ends. Now the intestine dries up from the beginning of the fistula, and you see drying both the probe, and it should be inside the fistula until the section reaches the place to which the end of the probe extends; and by means of the probe it is freed and treated.
And then cleanse those parts of the body that are affected by fistulas, which resemble an owl feather quill tube, and do not damage any part without cause.
But if blood flows when you are operating on those parts of the body affected by fistulas, then the thread and the sharp instrument should be cauterized with fire or with a strong medicine, for cauterizing with fire adjusts two good habits: it tightens the adjusted flesh and stops the bleeding by removing excess moisture.
And then treat that with bandages soaked in cold water or in a thrice-prepared concoction until the area feels better, and afterwards treat the wound with hard flesh-producing remedies which generate and strengthen.
And medicines that have the properties of being styptic and drying; when these are restored, it is healed and you need not fear recurrence.
But if the fistula has penetrated inside the anal region and is long from the surface of the body, then insert your finger into the anus and examine it.
And thus if you feel the probe and between it and your finger there is a membrane of leather or flesh, and it is prepared for penetration, then no operation should be performed there except according to faith and hope.

Regarding the stitching of hemorrhoids in which pus flows during the incision of those areas.
Hemorrhoids exist in two types: either they appear around the anus like coal lumps, or they are soft and resemble grape bunches. On the treatment of plagues.
I have already stated in the division of the treatment of plagues what was appropriate for the book, and I will now describe the treatment with both medicines according to their properties.
Therefore, I say that plagues are diverse depending on what causes the plagues and according to the place where the plaques appear.
And the causes for which such wounds are made as stone throwing, or cutting with a sword or knife, or striking with a lance, or with a stick, or with an arrow, or similar to these various causes.
But plagues that occur in different parts of the body such as a plague that affects the head, the neck, the feet, the abdomen, the groin, and similar parts of the limbs.
And I recommend the treatment of certain plagues by applying that reasoning and rule to other plagues as well.
And I will begin with simple plagues of the head, for the treatment of compound plagues will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Then say that when you encounter a simple wound on the head and it is not a fracture, at that moment consider: if it happened from throwing of a stone or similar object, and the skin has been broken only and there is a large bruise and you fear for that patient having a dangerous abscess, then immediately treat them by opening a vein to let blood, and do not delay this; and extract as much blood from them according to the quantity necessary based on the strength of the person unless some cause prohibits letting blood, especially if the blood coming out of the wound is little.
And let the phlebotomy be from the opposite side of the wounded part; and protect the patient from overeating and from eating heavy foods.
But if some cause prohibits phlebotomy in such a minor case, then reduce the amount of food and do not allow meat or heavy foods.
And place a poultice on the wound, if an abscess develops, apply it with rose oil alone or with a substance that has been stypticized.
But if you are sure of a dangerous abscess, then place a poultice on the wound, if it is recent and while the blood is fresh and the air has not changed, use the powder that I recommend in small amounts.
And if the air has already changed at that time, then apply other remedies until it is healed.
But if the wound is large or caused by a sword or similar weapon, and the edges of the wound do not come together when pressed together, then approximate those edges with sutures as I recommend for suturing them.
But if the wound is already exposed to bone and sinew, and it does not require extensive support but only a small suspensorium, then incise it appropriately and treat the wound with medicines and restore the flesh in place of the skin. Instruct the patient to eat foods that are light: fish and similar foods until they recover.
And if you find in the wound putrefaction and it does not adhere to the bone, then you cut away all that is purulent and remove it, and afterwards treat it.
And if in these wounds an artery or vein from which blood can flow is present, and it cannot be stopped with medicines, then you inquire about the artery, and if you find that which has not been cut, then you cut that with a scalpel, or tie that; and if necessity provokes that what we have said does not suffice, then you cauterize so that the blood is stopped.
And if these wounds are simple and small, then the cause of them is slight; therefore, you powder over those this powder, for it will consolidate them before the air changes them.
And the method of the powder is as follows: take oil from henbane one part, blood of dragon two parts, and burnt frankincense three parts; mix all thoroughly and sift it, and fill the wound with it, and bind it well with good compression so that it adheres to the dressing, and let it coagulate with the blood.
And then bind that above the powders and leave it, and do not loosen it while it remains such that it is not inflamed, for the medicine will not be effective within it until it is healed.
And sometimes this is done solely with cautery, when henbane and dragon's blood are not available to you.
And this method of treatment is used for large wounds when it is necessary to lay them open and narrow them, and for fresh wounds with their blood, which the air has not altered.
And if the air has altered them, and especially when it is in summer time, do not apply the position of this powder then, but treat those with what we have said, namely placing on those some warm compresses of boiled wheat, or place on those flour of barley mixed with water and honey until they rot; and afterwards treat those with another treatment until they are healed.
But if it happens that there is a fracture in the bone, and it is small, then you extract that with wheat.

Of the ailments of the neck.

If the vertebrae of the neck or entirely have been cut, and if the veins of the neck remain intact, then you should close the edges of the wound with sutures over the trachea without touching it; first equalize it and reduce it to its natural shape, and subsequently strengthen it with proper dressing, and leave it for several days; afterwards treat it with remedies that have astringent and excitatory properties until it is healed.
If the wound has already penetrated into the bone, then probe it, and if there are fragments of bone in it, extract all that you can from them; and what does not seem appropriate to you, leave it until the wound suppuses and separates on its own.

If it is a wound from a lance or a knife, and you feel the depth of it, then consider whether there is air in the wound when the patient inhales; then you will know that the wound is fatal.
And if there is no depth in the wound and it is fresh with its own blood, then for the first hour you should apply powder to it, and do not tighten it so that the blood does not remain trapped within the depths of the wound and return to the heart and poison the patient, but rather apply an attractive poultice to it twice a day.
And if the poultice is not available to you, then apply a cloth over the wound opening so that it absorbs what remains of the moisture; and have the patient lie on the wound so that whatever is adhered to it can run out.
But if three days or more have already passed since the wound appeared and no spasms, tremors of the heart, or constriction of breath occur to the patient, and you see other good signs from it, then you will know that the wound is safe; and then treat it with dressings and other treatments until it is healed.
But if the healing of the wound is unnecessary and all the time it remains open, then you will know that a fistula has formed; treat it therefore according to its own chapter.
And if the wound is from a stab with a sword or knife and it is simple on the surface of the flesh or back, then treat it according to what requires stitching, if it is large, or with powder, if it is small.
But if it has already affected the bone and pieces of it are embedded in the wound, then you should turn the wound and try to extract those pieces, if they are separated. If they are not separated, then leave them inside until the swelling subsides, for their extraction is too difficult.
And for other swellings in the other members, the aid in treatment is the aid of what we have said.
Of the swellings of the abdomen.
The discomfort that occurs in the abdomen is either great, little, or moderate.
And a small disruption is difficult to perform by another method, and it should be noted that the reduction of them is more difficult if not treated with an intervention to return them to their place immediately, as they become swollen and enlarged, making instruments difficult to use.
And therefore, the best disruption is moderate, for in that case the reduction of the belly band is not difficult, whereas it is difficult in both of the previous types mentioned.
And know that the suturing of the abdomen is done in four ways, but two of these sutures are common and suitable for suturing other swellings of the body.
And the two other specific sutures are also used for other swellings, but they are more specifically appropriate for the suturing of the abdomen.
And I recommend to you each one with explanation and declaration.
Therefore, I say that when the swelling is small and caused by some reason related to the belly band, and it is difficult to reduce it, then this happens in one of two ways: either due to the smallness of the disruption as we have said, or when the belly band becomes inflamed due to exposure to cold air.
Therefore, when it is thus, the time comes that you should scald that which is inflamed with a sponge or cloth moistened in pure water, or soaked in vinegar, and cyperum, and spica, and apply those to the bag so that the inflammation may be resolved.
And sometimes you will find this in one where there is styptic quality, and it is better than water alone for resolving the inflammation.
And when you see the inflammation resolved, now you moisten the bag with water in which chamomile and mallows are steeped, for by this the instrument of healing is made pleasant with little cause.
But if the instrument of healing is excused near this treatment, now you should divide the abscess slightly with an instrument with which hemorrhoids are incised.
And the first treatment is better, when it is appropriate that there be no drying, and it not be necessary to dry in proximity due to need and deficiency.
Regarding the instrument, this is its form:
One part of it is sharp-pointed, and the other part is blunt, with a delicate tip, but not as fine as a spatula; rather, it should be slightly rounded.
And when the swelling is enlarged and you remove the bag, now it is necessary that its reduction be according to its natural form in its proper place, if possible in that manner, for it is better.
But when the abscess is wide and it is in the lower part of the abdomen, now it is necessary that you have the patient lie on their back, and place their legs further apart than their head; and if it is in the upper part of the abdomen, then you should place their head and feet higher than the lower parts.
And so if the rupture is in one of the two parts of the abdomen, then pause your intention and your consideration entirely for this, so that the part in which the ailment is may be lower than the other.
And so you should administer this in major ailments and in minor ailments.
And in minor ailments, pause what is prepared by you, and then have it administered by one of your most trusted assistants, who should hold the rupture entirely with their hand and adjust the lips, and then uncover to proceed with suturing at some appropriate time.
And this is the common method of suturing: take a needle, or an equivalent to a needle according to the quantity and amplitude of the wound; then leave from the extremity of the rupture with your ring finger, and tighten the needle once, ensuring that you do not insert pins at both ends of the thread, but rather at both ends of the tissue that is below the edges of the wound; until you make it penetrate into that part; and when you have already joined both ends of the thread and both ends of the tissue, thus making four knots.
And then tighten around the needle with double knots, and do this from both sides repeatedly, and then join the two lips of the wound together appropriately; and then use the thickness of your finger to guide another needle into it, and then tie that one off with a knot just as you did with the first needle; and do not stop doing this if necessary with additional needles until you have completed the entire closure of the wound.
And the needles should be of medium thickness between coarseness and fineness, for fine needles penetrate the flesh too quickly; and coarse ones are difficult to insert into the tissue, so they should be of medium fineness and thickness.
I must not say that the needle should be placed at both ends of the bone in question, so that the flesh is not cut too quickly and the wound has time to heal before consolidation.
And they should not be extended with stitches so that the wound is not prevented from consolidating.
And when cutting the ends of the needles, do so in such a way that they do not protrude and cause discomfort to the patient lying down; and place cotton pads over the stitches, which should cover the ends of the needles; leave them like this until you know that the wound has already healed.
And in these cases of stitching, it is most convenient to use needles in such a way that for small wounds, only one needle or two may suffice.
But the second stitching is common: it involves applying stitches to the four ends of the wound, including both ends of the bone and two extremities of the sinew, at once, with a needle that is carefully wrapped in fineness and thickness.
And when you have penetrated these four extremities with the needle, withdraw the needle from that part where you began, so that the thread is drawn back to the most prominent part of the wound, so that the stitching will be like a second layer of fabric, tightly securing it.
And place each stitch about the thickness of your smallest finger apart.
And this stitching method is known to surgeons.
And with such stitching, I closed a wound in the abdomen of a man who was stabbed with a knife, where the tear in the wound was larger than one palm, and it had penetrated the intestines about two palms from the small intestine, and the disruption was in the middle part; then I reduced it after the intestine had protruded from the wound for twenty-four hours.
And the wound is consolidated in the space of fifteen days or thereabouts, and he covers it with bandages, and it is healed; and afterwards let him exercise the limb gently, and it will return to its proper condition.
And the other doctors judged that he would not be healed; and by a miracle of fire, for I did not cover that wound with any bandage, since it was in a place where no one could reach or apply any medicine, but placed over the wound two pieces of cloth daily moistened with honeyed water until it was healed.
But I will describe two species of suture according to the narrative of Paulus.
And it is that you begin the suture from the edge, and insert the needle from the outer part to the inner part.
And thus as the needle penetrates at the edge and in that place tie knots according to straightness and length of the whole body, and leave the end of the thread in which you have inserted the needle; and make the needle penetrate at the other end from the inner part to the outer part at the other end of the wound.
And when you have made that penetration, then make another penetration in the same end of the wound from the outer part to the inner part; and leave the end of the thread that is in this place, and make the needle penetrate at the other end from the inner part to the outer part.
And make that penetration such that when you penetrate with the thread at its end on the side where all of it will be inside, it penetrates properly.
Here begins the method for this technique, which starts at the extremity that is on one side of the suture and removes the needle that penetrates there. Then place it in that loop and attach the end of the suture that is on the other side to this extremity; then remove it from the loop that is nearby.
And do this one side and then the other, and do this alternately with each stitch as you sew all of what is outside according to that example.
The sum of this method of suturing is that you sew with a suture needle as you would when sewing skins, thus you sew the suture one side from the loop end, and leave the other side until it is complete.
The second kind of suture which is called "Gualia" and which they recommend for it, is that you sew it similarly to how some physicians do it, thus adding each part to its corresponding part naturally; and they join the end of one to the end of the other opposite side, and this is done as I tell you.
Place the needle at the end of the suture on your right side of the outer part, and make it penetrate into the inner part in that spot, leaving two ends of the suture free; then rotate the needle and make it pass from outside to inside through the two ends of the suture.
Then rotate each one, and make them penetrate from the inner part into the outer part through two other ends of the suture on the opposite side.
And this method of suture is better than the common light suture, and it is the suture of which a prior mention is recalled.
This is the speech of Walia.
And if someone were to say that the suture of the abdomen is done with two needles, it is such that you insert a pin into each of them, and begin by inserting one needle according to what you need to do, and make that penetrate within the other side according to the suturing method of those who sew clothes in the same manner.
And you should know that when the disruption is in the middle part of the abdomen, then the suture of it is more difficult than that of other parts of the abdomen.

But if you do not have the medicines at hand, then apply something to it immediately, as it begins to get hot and becomes inflamed, and change that twice a day, as you have been taught, until it is healed, since you will not need other medication for such simple wounds in most cases.

And if pain or putrefaction occurs in the abdominal organs, since this is likely to happen, then you should apply styptic black tibetan medicine to it, and especially if the putrefaction has reached the organ and an incision must be made penetrating into its cavity.

Remembrance of the troubles that occur in the bowel.
When disruption occurs in the bowel and is small, it is possible that it can be repaired in some people, because I saw one who had been wounded in the belly by a lance thrust, and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and the wound was old and had formed a fistula, with discharge and gas.
Then I bandaged the area without being confident in its healing, but tried to alleviate that part which was healing and where the tissue was consolidating.
And when I saw the area already consolidated, I feared the damage that could arise from this bad event in his belly; and no one suffered any harm from this accident by keeping to their usual food and drink habits, and soon they were bathing and exercising as usual.
And some experienced people say that when there is a small wound in the bowel, it should be treated as follows: take ants with large heads; then bring together the edges of the wound and place one of those ants, with its mouth open, on the edges of the wound. When the ant bites down on them, cut off its head because it will stick and not dissolve.
And then place another ant next to the first one, and do not stop placing ants one after another according to the quantity of the entire wound.
And then reduce that and close the wound; and let those heads remain in the bowel until the bowel is healed; and no harm will come to the patient.
It is possible that the purse [surgical ligature] be made of fine gut, which is made from the gut of an animal and is as thin as a needle; and it is that you take the end of this gut, and it should be bare, and join the end of it to the fine gut, wrapped around, and then thread that gut on needles and sew it to that purse, and reduce it at the division.
And this method of suturing with ants is nothing but a second way of trust and hope.
But if the wound is large and wide, especially if it is in one of the fine guts, then at that time there can be only a partial healing, and not a complete healing of it.
On the treatment of abscesses and fistulas.
Know that every wound and abscess when it is not healed properly and becomes old, and forms an ulcer, and does not heal completely over time and is not excised, then wherever in the body it may be, it is universally called a fistula, and we call it that same abscess.
And a fistula, in truth, is a felted node, hard and white, at which there is no pain but rather itching, just as the itch of goose flesh is; and for this reason it is called that raised spot, that is, an irritation.
And it is in some people moist, which flows continuously; and the moisture is excised within a few hours. And at times this moisture is moved, and it is little, and it is thick, and it is thin.
I have shown all those causes, the signs of them, and their cure with medicines in the division.
And it is fitting that I tell you about the treatment of fistulas, which is performed through an operation with my methods.
And you should know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; some of them affect large veins and arteries, others nerves, or the brain, or the intestines, or the bladder, or one of the ribs, or one of the vertebrae of the back, or one of the compound joints such as those of the hand and foot; and among these are those that occur near the main part of the limb and similar areas.
And therefore, among these fistulas that follow this method, they are among the illnesses difficult to heal, and do not receive a cure, and occupy much labor and ignorance.
And if any of the fistulas has a depth that does not reach the places mentioned above and you hope for and trust in its cure and wish to gain knowledge of it, then take a probe of iron or steel, and if the fistula runs straight ahead, explore it with this.
And if the fistula is tortuous, then investigate it with a probe of thin lead, for the lightness of lead's nature makes it easy and flexible around the tortuosity.
And if the fistula has openings that are frightening, it is not within your power to signify upon them with a probe.
Then irrigate the openings through those openings, for the moisture with which you irrigate will go to the other openings and flow from them.
And then inquire meticulously to determine if there is bone or nerve here, and whether the depth of the fistula is distant or near, or if it is a fistula with such openings that are beyond your full strength, your complete investigation, and your understanding of the disease and pain beneath your compression on the area, and similar signs and accidental causes related to the abscess.
And when you have stood firm on all those causes with true judgment, then proceed to the cure with confidence: consider whether the fistula is an apparent one that is near or in a clean location, distant from joints, nerves, arteries, veins, or any of the places I have told you about.
Now you should treat the fistula as described in its narration beforehand, and remove what is in that filtration and of corrupted flesh, and what has grown out from the skin opening or similar places, and care for it until it is healed.
If the fistula is of great depth and follows a straight course, it is necessary to incise it as far forward as you can, and then remove all the corrupted flesh; then apply plasters wrapped in sharp medicines, and insert them into the cavity of the fistula which you have probed with iron.
And do this for several days until the sharp medicine has dissolved everything that is rotten in the cavity of the fistula from corruption.
And then treat it with applications that generate healthy flesh until it is healed.
But if it does not heal with this treatment, then you should cauterize it as we have recommended.
But if the cause of the fistula is bone and you must determine this, then you should explore it and dry it out as we have recommended, unless you prohibit any involvement with a vein or nerve or major limb as we have said.
But if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness on it, then you should cut that away until all the corruption is removed; and then treat it with what promotes flesh until it is healed.
And if it does not heal and pus continues to discharge as before, then you will know that you have not reached complete removal of the corruption; and then uncover it again and carefully examine and clean it with the utmost care, and then treat it.
And if it heals, that is good; but if not, then you will know that the corruption is in the deep recesses of the body, which you have not reached, and then you must content yourself with treating that.
And if the corrupted bone is small, it is possible for you to remove that; then you should pull it out with fine forceps, which are suitable for this purpose.
And if small pieces of bone remain, then carefully remove all of them, and do not leave any behind for any reason due to your strength.
But if any cause of moisture opposes you, and in their incision there is neither fear nor hesitation, then incise those ligaments or muscles if necessary, and free the bones.
But if it is not the right time for you to remove the bones at this moment, then apply what can ease the swelling over the wound, and leave it open until such a time when there is flesh and ligaments around those bones, and guard against the healing of the wound so that it does not become consolidated, and keep the section that you have incised during your operation constricted.
Having said that, if you fear to proceed, apply a cloth soaked in warm oil or Egyptian ointment, or any of the green ointments, because when these muscles have relaxed, and the bones are separated from them, and their attachment is loosened.
But if it is a large bone such as the bone of a camel or ox or similar, and what is corrupted of it is only its surface, then scrape off that corruption only from behind until the blackness and corruption are removed, and subsequently restore the wound.
But if what is corrupted of it is a large part, and the corruption has already reached the marrow of the bone, then it is necessary to close that area and completely excise it where the corruption has spread, and subsequently treat it until it is consolidated.

A young man by age around xxx years, to whom it happens that he feels pain in his abdomen, and of the parts inside there is an injury concerning the matter inside the body through which the matter reaches the abdomen, and this matter forms into a large abscess, and it is not due to an external cause.

Regarding the cutting of extremities and the sawing of bones.
Extremities may need to be removed either due to an intrinsic cause or an extrinsic cause, or if you have treated that corruption with the cure of those medicines and the treatment does not help, or sometimes the corruption spreads to a limb without any apparent reason; in such cases, it is necessary for you to cut off that limb at the point where the corruption reaches, so that the patient may escape from death or severe illness, which would be a greater harm to the body.
And the sign of that which befalls one is that the member becomes black until it is cauterized so that fire has consumed it, or else you may approach the blackness until that corruption there in that member kills it and takes hold of the entire body; and thus cautery should be applied to it.
And similarly, this is caused by the percussion of certain poisonous causes, such as from a scorpion, sea creature, viper, or Russell's viper and similar ones.
And if the corruption or percussion is at the extremity of the finger, then you should incise the finger and not give space for the corruption to advance into the hand.
And similarly, if it affects the hand, then you should incise at the base of the joint and not give space for the corruption to advance into the elbow of the arm.
And if it spreads to that part, then you should incise the arm at the shoulder joint.
And if the corruption passes to another part and surrounds the shoulder, then that is the death of the patient; and administering another cause for this condition in treatment is a matter of proper dosage.
And similarly, do this for the foot when corruption spreads to the toe; then you should incise it between two of the joints.
And if it affects the sole of the foot, then you should incise the entire foot. But if it spreads to the toenail, then you should incise the toe at the joint of the toenail.
And if the corruption has already reached the bone, then at this point there is no remedy but dismissal, and leaving the patient to die.
And the method of incising or tying off an extremity is that you bind a ligature below the part where you wish to cut, and place another ligature above the location; extend one ligature towards the lower parts, and extend another towards the upper; then separate the flesh which lies between two ligatures with a spatula until all the flesh is exposed; then it may be incised or tied off.
And it is necessary to cover the area with a cloth from all sides so that it does not touch the affected site, and to ensure that the patient receives appropriate care and treatment for abscesses.
But if bleeding occurs while you are working, then you should cauterize the site immediately, or apply some powders to staunch the blood; and then return to your treatment until it is complete.
And then bind the injured limb with bandages where appropriate, and care for it until it is healed.

And that corruption spreads initially in his finger and then tends to affect the entire body.

On the treatment of hemorrhoids and the quality of enemas with medicines.
When an abscess occurs in some fleshy members and the space of the abscess extends so that there is a collection of pus, and then it ruptures and opens, and the pus is discharged from it, leaving the area empty as if it were a vessel, and the membrane above it remains thin like cloth, and has not reached corruption, nor does it affect bones or nerves or ligaments, it is called a hemorrhoid, and it is not named a fistula.
However, if the space extends so that corruption affects some member, it is then called a fistula and not a hemorrhoid.
And in the treatment of this, incise that wound entirely as it is revolved, and especially when it is thinned out and made like cloth, and ensure that it does not adhere to the place because of its corruption.
But if you hope that the wound will adhere and that such corruption has not yet reached its final consequence, and there is a passage in the wound, then now treat it with an enema.
And you must consider the smell, and now if it is strong, and the arm that you use has a fetid odor, then give an enema with Egyptian medicine, which consists of oil, vinegar, and saffron in equal parts, and mix them over fire until the medicine becomes thick and reaches the consistency of honey.
And then take what is necessary and dissolve it in water and honey; and give an enema with that for the smell, and stretch the opening of it, and leave the medicine inside for the duration of two hours.
And then extract that medicine with care; and do this for several days until the smell is cleansed and the corruption is removed.
And sometimes an enema is given with ash water when this medicine is not available to you; and you should take the ashes of wheat, put them over water; then strain it and give an enema with that until you are certain that the wound now is clean.
And if the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or ash water, then give an enema with water and honey mixed equally three times, and give an enema with vinegar and honey mixed, for the property of honey cleanses and washes, and vinegar makes the wound adhere, especially when the vinegar has a surplus of styptic and drying properties.
And when you see that some wounds are swollen and you confirm that the sinus is already drained, then irrigate those with water that promotes flesh growth.
And it is that you take a decoction of white oak bark and dissolve it with rose oil and vine stiptic; or what you irrigate with some medicines and other decoctions which have the properties already written in the chapter on decoctions.
And if the orifice of the sinus is narrow and does not allow the cannula of the irrigation to pass through, then you should gradually enlarge it with a small instrument, and pause while wrapping it in a decoction of Egyptian herbs or basilicon decoction until it is enlarged.
And similarly, if the orifice is wide, then you should suture the edges of it and leave a quantity through which the irrigation can pass.
And if the orifice from which the pus flows is raised to the upper parts, then dry it in the lower part where the pus can flow downward, for when the pus is obstructed in the depth of the sinus, flesh will be generated there.
And if it is not possible for you to dry the sinus near the lower bone as you wish, then make sure to prepare the member in such a way that the pus flows easily according to your ability and that there is no obstruction preventing the flow of the pus.
May he who is above the opening of the sinus, which you should probe at all times so that what is lodged in it may come out. And so that you may know whether what flows from the wound is fresh blood or clotted, or digested, or undigested.
And for this reason you should consider the location of that sinus, whether the patient feels pain there or not, and whether it is in an abscess.
And when your treatment is prolonged in this manner, and you see that the matter that has been discharged over the opening of the sinus adheres or tends to adhere, then you should loosen it on the third day, and when you loosen the crust, then change the cloth for another and renew the dressing.
But if within the sinus there is space for subtle pus, then do not despair of its adhesion, for healing will be appropriate, because some people in whom flesh grows slowly on their wounds, and similarly with those in whom the opposite occurs.
And if for many days the wound remains undigested and full of pus, then you know that the sinus does not adhere; and if the adhesion of the sinus is delayed and becomes prolonged, then adjust to a drying effect of the medicines, and if the medicines are moist in their substance and in their virtue, they should be dried as well when applied, for there is an excess of moisture to be reduced.
And the most important thing for healing is to take a drying dressing and dissolve it in rose oil, and apply it over the wound along with an earlier ointment in its substance, and see how that works on it, and use it accordingly.
It appears in that action, when there is no bandage, they find a piece of cloth, honey when it has been cooked so that it becomes thickened, and use it; or take myrrh and aloes and pound them, and sprinkle all over the honey which is on the fire, and then spread this over linen and stretch that over the wound; and spread that with the honey in which you have cooked until it was thickened, and sprinkle over cloth and stretch that.

And if the wound is prolonged and has not been healed by this treatment, now you know that the corruption is in the core of it, and it makes an inquiry in the bones or in the other hard members or in the ligaments; now treat it with fistula treatment, as mentioned above.
On the treatment of blisters, cracked nails, and the cutting and division of a finger.
A blister is an abscess that arises from under the nail of a toe or finger, and it can also arise in other fingers. When it prolongs and its treatment is more difficult, it may be an abscess caused by cautery, or it may become corrupt. It secretes pus internally which corrodes the root of the nail, and quickly corrupts the entire area. Its corruption often reaches the bone causing a foul odor, and the extremity of the finger becomes blackened, and its color turns dark.
Therefore, when you have the instrument in water as we have said in the division and do not compress your treatment, then it is necessary that you incise with iron all the excess that is swollen from the nail and immediately cauterize the wound nearby, for cauterization is helpful in such cases.
But if the bone is exposed and the nail is healthy, and the addictions of the nail withdraw and compress the flesh inward, and begin to press upon that spot, then it is necessary for you to apply a fine probe below the angle of the nail that presses on the flesh, and urge it up and incise that flesh with ease, and place over what remains of the flesh corrosive medicines until it is completely removed; and then cure that area with applications until it is healed.
But if the corruption has already penetrated into the bone, then it is necessary for you to incise the bone and extract it, for it is never healed when there is corruption in the bone.

On the incision of veins, so are varicose veins.
Veins are varicose veins, and they are thick-walled veins filled with excess melancholic humors that flow to the limbs of the body, and the greatest accumulation of these occurs in the legs, especially in the legs of travelers, workers, and carriers.
Then it is necessary that you administer purgatives from the black bile of the body several times with strong expulsion, and subsequently let blood from the patient from the basilic vein.
However, the treatment for them is according to two methods: one is that they are incised and the black blood is drawn out, and the other method is that the vein is raised and completely removed.
The sectioning is done in this manner: first, apply hot water to the leg so that the thick blood is dissolved, which is a sediment in the leg, and then tightly bind the leg with bandages at the part above the knee and below the calf, and then tie off the vein at one place or two, or three with wide ligatures, and then draw out the black blood with your hand from below the leg upwards, until the amount of blood is removed that you want and that suffices for what the strength of the patient can tolerate.
And then bind it tightly, and command the patient to abstain from foods that generate black bile.
And repeat the treatment with phlebotomy when the veins are full, and inform the patient about this.
However, the raising of them is according to this method: you should shave the leg of the patient if it has hair on it, and then put him in hot water so that his leg turns red and the veins become prominent; or exercise it vigorously with physical activity if a bath is not available, until the limb becomes warm.
From the side of the neck cut open the vein on the right by section either in front or at the back of it, or lower down sever the tendon.
Near the shoulder use hooks and strip the vein from all parts until it appears to the touch, and you should recognize its appearance when you see that part turning black.
And thus as you expose it and from the neck you see that white one which is the tendon.
And then place the ligature below where it is elevated and detached from the neck, and suspend it with hooks or threads.
And then make another incision near that incision at three points, and then strip the neck from above the vein until it appears.
And then elevate that and incise it at the rear section where the tendon is, and then extract that and elevate it until it passes through the second incision, and then extract it from the incision above that.
And do this until you extract it from the incision that is highest or farthest from all the incisions, until everything has passed through; and now cut it.
And if it does not obey you to extract and elevate it, now insert a needle with a strong double thread and ligature it and extract it, or place the ligature below it and rotate your hand in all directions until it is dislodged. And be careful that it is not cut; for if it is broken, it will be difficult for you to elevate it, and blame will come upon you for this harm.
And when all the air has been expelled, then place on the wound a cloth submerged in wine and rose oil and non-rose oil, and treat it until it is healed.

On cutting into worms generated under the skin and it is called bovine illness.
This illness is named in some lands as cattle disease because often seen among cows and it is a worm that has been born between the skin and flesh, which moves throughout the body up and down, and is revealed through sensation due to its movement from limb to limb until it breaks through the skin and comes out.
And its generation is from the putrefaction of certain humors, just as happens with worms, serpents, and parasites in the belly.
And it is feared because of its malice, for when it moves in the body and rises to the head, and reaches the brain, then suddenly it becomes heavy and enters there, destroying the brain, which often leads to many deaths.
And so when you want to cure that and extract it, then it is done only according to its wandering movement and appearance to the senses. You must press on what is above it and what is below it with binding and constriction, and then dry over it and extract it.
